Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Wasiyyah: Linguistic and Legal Meanings with Eight Aspects
Defining wasiyyah linguistically and legally with eight aspects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define wasiyyah in Hanafi fiqh, distinguish its linguistic and legal meanings, and explain why the standard definition is considered incomplete by the commentator.

Core Idea
Wasiyyah is a deferred transfer of ownership after death, but that definition must also include rights of Allah and debts to be comprehensive.

In this lesson, we explore the definition of wasiyyah from the Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author not only provides the standard definition—tamlik mudaf li ma ba'd al-mawt—but also critiques it for omitting key components like expiations and unpaid debts. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the rules of bequests, especially when a testator leaves instructions beyond simple transfer of assets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning of wasiyyah
The term wasiyyah is derived from tawsiyah, meaning recommendation or instruction. It is used as a verbal noun in the Quran.
Quran 5:106 uses the phrase 'at the time of wasiyyah'.
2
Identify the legal definition in the Hanafi school
The standard legal definition is 'tamlik mudaf li ma ba'd al-mawt' – a transfer of ownership attached to after death, by way of donation, whether in assets or usufruct.
This is the definition found in the base text and many commentaries.
3
Note the eight aspects of wasiyyah
The commentator enumerates eight aspects: linguistic interpretation, legal interpretation, reason for legislation, pillar, condition, description, ruling, and evidence. Only the first two are elaborated in this passage.
These aspects provide a comprehensive framework for understanding wasiyyah.
4
Analyze the author's critique of the standard definition
The author argues that the standard definition is not comprehensive because it excludes rights of Allah (e.g., expiations) and debts. He suggests adding 'or a request for discharge of liabilities' to cover these cases.
The critique aims to include non-tamlik instructions under the umbrella of wasiyyah.
5
Understand the defense of the standard definition
Some later scholars defend the use of 'or' in definitions, allowing a single definition to encompass multiple types. The standard definition remains core, but the critique shows the need for a broader understanding.
The definition evolves to include both transfer and request for discharge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا الوصية تمليك مضاف لما بعد الموت. قال الشراح: إيراد كتاب الوصايا في آخر الكتاب ظاهر المناسبة إذ آخر الأحوال في الآدمي في الدنيا الموت والوصية معاملة وقت الموت أقول : برد عليه أن كتاب الوصايا ليس بمورود في آخر هذا الكتاب وإنما المورود في آخره كتاب الخنثى كما ترى نعم أن كثير أصحاب التصانيف أوردوه في آخر كتبهم لكن الكلام في شرح هذا الكتاب، ويمكن من الجواب من قبل الشراح حمل الآخر في قولهم في آخر الكتاب على الإضافي فإن آخره الحقيقي وإن كان كتاب الخنثى إلا أن كتاب الوصايا أيضاً آخره بالإضافة إلى ما قبله حيث قرب آخره الحقيقي، ومن هذا ترى القوم يقولون وقع هذا في أوائل كذا أو أواخره فإن صيغة الجمع لا تتمشى في الأول الحقيقي والآخر الحقيقي وإنما المخلص في الأول والآخر الحقيقي والإضافي. والكلام في الوصية من وجوه: الأول في تفسيرها لغة . والثاني في تفسيرها شرعاً والثالث في سبب المشروعية والرابع في ركنها. والخامس في شرطها. والسادس في صفتها والسابع في حكمها. والثامن في دليل مشروعيتها. أما الوصية في اللغة فهي اسم بمعنى المصدر الذي هو التوصية ومنه قوله تعالى : وحين الوصية [المائدة : ١٠٦] ثم الموصى به وصية ومنه قوله تعالى : من بعد وصية توصون بها [النساء : ١٢] وفي الشريعة الوصية تمليك مضاف لما يعد الموت بطريق التبرع سواء كانت في الأعيان أو في المنافع ؛ كذا في عامة الشروح أقول وهذا التعريف ليس بجامع لأنه لا يشمل حقوق الله تعالى والدين الذي في ذمته ولو قال المؤلف هي طلب براءة ذمته من حقوق الله تعالى والعباد ما لم يصلهما أو تمليك إلى الآخره لكان أولى. لا يقال إدخال أو في الحدود لا يجوز لأن الحدود الحقيقية ولا تعدد فيها لأنا نقول : إذا أريد تعريف الحقيقة في ضمن الأفراد جاز ذلك كما تقرر . قال بعض المتأخرين : ثم الوصية والتوصية وكذا الإيصاء اللغة طلب فعل من غيره ليفعله في غيبته حال حياته أو بعد وفاته. وفي الشريعة تمليك ذلك في سمی
Book of Wasiyyah. The wasiyyah is a deferred transfer of ownership to after death. The commentators said: Bringing the book of wasiyyah at the end of the book is apparently appropriate, since the last state of a human in the world is death, and wasiyyah is a transaction at the time of death. I say: This is refuted by the fact that the book of wasiyyah is not placed at the end of this book; rather, what is placed at its end is the book of the hermaphrodite, as you see. Yes, many authors placed it at the end of their books, but the discussion is about the commentary on this book. A possible answer from the commentators is that they meant 'last' in a relative sense, for although the real end is the book of the hermaphrodite, the book of wasiyyah is also last relative to what comes before it, since it is near the real end. From this you see people say 'this occurred in the beginnings or ends of such-and-such', because the plural form does not apply to the real first and real last; rather, the solution is in the real and relative first and last. The discussion of wasiyyah has eight aspects: first, its linguistic interpretation; second, its legal interpretation; third, the reason for its legislation; fourth, its pillar; fifth, its condition; sixth, its description; seventh, its ruling; eighth, the evidence for its legislation. As for wasiyyah linguistically, it is a noun meaning the verbal noun which is tawsiyah, and from it is the verse 'at the time of wasiyyah' (Quran 5:106). Then the bequeathed item is called wasiyyah, and from it is the verse 'after a wasiyyah which you bequeath' (Quran 4:12). In shari'ah, wasiyyah is a deferred transfer of ownership to after death by way of donation, whether in specific assets or in usufruct; thus in all the commentaries. I say: This definition is not comprehensive because it does not include the rights of Allah and the debt that is on the deceased. If the author had said: 'It is a request for the acquittal of his liability from the rights of Allah and the people if he did not fulfill them, or a transfer to after death', it would be better. It cannot be said that including 'or' in definitions is not allowed, because real definitions are not multiple; we say: If one intends to define the reality within individuals, it is permissible, as established. Some later scholars said: Then wasiyyah, tawsiyah, and also isa' linguistically are requesting an action from another to do it in his absence during his life or after his death. In shari'ah, it is a transfer of that...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the definition of wasiyyah from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It opens with a discussion on why the book of wasiyyah is placed near the end of the original text, noting that commentators justify it as relative placement. The author then enumerates eight aspects of wasiyyah: linguistic definition, legal definition, reason for legislation, pillar, condition, description, ruling, and evidence. He provides the standard Hanafi definition: a deferred transfer of ownership (tamlik mudaf) to take effect after death by way of donation, covering both assets and usufruct. However, he criticizes this definition as non-comprehensive because it omits rights of Allah (e.g., expiations) and unpaid debts. He suggests a more inclusive definition using 'or' to cover both transfer and request for discharge. He defends the use of 'or' in definitions by distinguishing between defining a single essence and listing its types. The passage ends with a quote from later scholars differentiating the linguistic meaning (request to do something in absence) from the legal meaning (transfer). This lesson guards against over-narrow definitions that exclude essential components like debts.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-waṣiyyah): In language: a name for the masdar meaning recommendation. In shari'ah: a deferred transfer of ownership (tamlik) to take effect after death, as a donation, whether in specific assets or usufruct.
تمليك مضاف (tamlik muḍāf): A transfer of ownership that is attached (muḍāf) to a future time, here after death.
التوصية (al-tawṣiyah): Synonym for wasiyyah; also means instructing someone to do something in one's absence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's critique, what is missing from the standard legal definition of wasiyyah (tamlik mudaf li ma ba'd al-mawt)?
A) The requirement of acceptance
B) Rights of Allah and debts
C) The condition of one-third
D) The evidence from Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of wasiyyah as a deferred transfer of ownership must be understood to also encompass the discharge of rights and debts for completeness.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
beginner
8 min
The Definition and Legal Nature of Wasiyya
Defines wasiyya linguistically and legally, discusses its cause and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of a will (wasiyya) and distinguish between its linguistic and legal meanings, including the cause (sabab) for its legislation.

Core Idea
A will is a deferred transfer of ownership after death, permitted by istihsan despite qiyas disapproving.

This lesson opens the chapter on wills from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author begins by explaining the placement of the chapter, then provides a rigorous definition of wasiyya, both linguistically and legally, drawing on Quranic evidence. He also critiques earlier definitions and clarifies the cause (sabab) for legislating wills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and legal definitions
Read the definitions given: linguistic meaning from Quran verses (5:106, 4:12), and the legal definition as 'tamlīk muḍāf limā ba‘d al-mawt ʿalā sabīl al-tabarruʿ'.
The legal definition is common in Hanafi commentaries.
2
Analyze the author's critique of the legal definition
The author argues the standard definition is insufficient because it excludes rights of Allah and debts. He suggests adding 'rights of Allah and debts' or using a disjunctive definition.
This shows the precision expected in later Hanafi scholarship.
3
Distinguish the two meanings of 'wasiyya'
According to some later scholars, 'wasiyya' has two meanings: (1) requesting something after one's death (with preposition 'li'), and (2) the actual deferred transfer (with preposition 'ila').
This resolves why some topics like debts are included in the book of wills.
4
State the cause (sabab) of the will
The cause is the desire for good repute in this world and high ranks in the Hereafter, similar to other donations.
The sabab explains why the act is recommended.

المورود في آخرة كتاب الخنثى كما ترى نعم أن كثير أصحاب التصانيف أوردوه في آخر كتبهم لكن الكلام في شرح هذا الكتاب، ويمكن من الجواب من قبل الشراح حمل الآخر في قولهم في آخر الكتاب على الإضافي فإن آخره شرطها. والسادس في صفتها والسابع في حكمها. والثامن في دليل مشروعيتها. أما الوصية في اللغة فهي اسم بمعنى المصدر الذي هو التوصية ومنه قوله تعالى : ﴿حين الوصية﴾ [المائدة : ١٠٦] ثم الموصى به وصية ومنه قوله تعالى : ﴿من بعد وصية توصون بها﴾ [النساء : ١٢] وفي الشريعة الوصية تمليك مضاف لما يعد الموت بطريق التبرع سواء كانت في الأعيان أو في المنافع ؛ كذا في عامة الشروح أقول وهذا التعريف ليس بجامع لأنه لا يشمل حقوق الله تعالى والدين الذي في ذمته ولو قال المؤلف هي طلب براءة ذمته من حقوق الله تعالى والعباد ما لم يصلهما أو تمليك إلى الآخره لكان أولى. لا يقال إدخال أو في الحدود لا يجوز لأن الحدود الحقيقية ولا تعدد فيها لأنا نقول : إذا أريد تعريف الحقيقة في ضمن الأفراد جاز ذلك كما تقرر . قال بعض المتأخرين : ثم الوصية والتوصية وكذا الإيصاء اللغة طلب فعل من غيره ليفعله في غيبته حال حياته أو بعد وفاته. وفي بهذا المعنى هي المحكوم عليها بأنها مستحبة غير واجبة وأن القياس يأبى جوازها فعلى هذا يكون بعض المسائل مثل مسألة حقوق الله تعالى وحقوق العباد والمسائل المتعلقة بالوصي مذكورة في كتاب الوصايا بطريق التطفل الحسن في الدنيا ووصول الدرجات العالية في العقبي. وأما شرائطها فكون الموصي أهلاً للتبرع، وأن لا يكون مديوناً، وكون الموصى له حياً وقت الوصية وإن لم يكن مولوداً حتى إذا أوصى للجنين إذا كان موجوداً حياً عند الوصية تصح وإلا فلا. وإنما تعرف حياته في ذلك الوقت بأن ولدته قبل سنة أشهر حياً. وكونه أجنبياً حتى إن الوصية للوارث لا تجوز إلا بإجازة الورثة، وأن لا يكون قاتلاً، وكون الموصى به شيئاً قابلاً للتمليك من الغير بعقد من العقود حال حياة الموصي، سواء كان موجوداً في الحال أو معدوماً. وأن يكون أيضاً الموصى به بقدر الثلث حتى إنها لا تصح فيما زاد على الثلث؛ في النهاية. وفي العناية أيضاً بطريق الإجمال. وفي الأصل ومن شروطها كون الموصي أهلاً للتبرع فلا تصح من صبي ولا عبد. وأقول : فيه قصور بلا خلل؛ أما أولاً فلأنه جعل من شرائطها أن لا يكون الموصي مديوناً بدون التقييد بأن يكون الدين مستغرقاً لتركته والشرط عدم هذا الدين المقيد لا عدم الدين المطلق كما صرح به في البدائع وغيره. وأما ثانياً فلأنه جعل من شرائطها كون الموصى له حياً وقت الوصية والشرط كونه موجوداً وقت الوصية لا كونه حياً ألا ترى أنهم جعلوا الدليل عليه الولادة قبل ستة أشهر حياً وتلك إنما تدل على وجود الجنين وقت الوصية لا على حياته في ذلك الوقت كما لا يخفى على العارف بأحوال الجنين في الرحم وبأقل مدة الحمل، وعن هذا كان المذكور في عامة المعتبرات عند بيان هذا الشرط أن يكون الموصى له موجوداً وقت الوصية بدون ذكر قيد الحياة أصلاً. وأما ثالثاً فلأنه جعل من شرائطها أن يكون الموصى به مقدار الثلث لا زائداً عليه وهو ليس بسديد على إطلاقه فإن الموصي إذا ترك ورثه فإنما لا تصح وصيته بما زاد على الثلث إن لم تجز الورثة، وإن أجازوه صحت وصیته به. وأما إذا لم يترك وارثاً فتصح وصيته بما زاد على الثلث حتى بجميع ماله عندنا كما تقرر في موضعه فلا بد من التقييد مرتين مرة بأن يكون له وارث، وأخرى بأن لا يجيزه الوارث والله أعلم. وأما ركنها فقوله أوصيت بكذا.
Book of Wills. The will is a transfer of ownership deferred until after death. ... The scholars said: Placing the Book of Wills at the end of the book is apparently appropriate since the last condition of a human in this world is death, and the will is a transaction at the time of death. I say: It is objected that the Book of Wills is not placed at the end of this book; rather, what is placed at the end is the Book of the Hermaphrodite, as you see. Yes, many authors have placed it at the end of their books, but the discussion is about the commentary of this book. A response can be given from the commentators: they meant 'end' in a relative sense. ... The discussion about the will is from eight aspects: first, its linguistic interpretation; second, its legal interpretation; third, the reason for its legislation; fourth, its pillar; fifth, its condition; sixth, its description; seventh, its ruling; eighth, the proof of its legitimacy. As for the will linguistically, it is a noun meaning the verbal noun 'tawsiyah', and from it is the saying of Allah: 'at the time of the will' [5:106]. Then the bequeathed thing is called a will, and from it is His saying: 'after a will you make' [4:12]. In Shari'ah, the will is a transfer of ownership deferred until after death by way of donation, whether in specific objects or benefits; thus in all commentaries. I say: This definition is not comprehensive because it does not include the rights of Allah and the debt owed by the testator. ... The cause of the will is the cause of all donations, which is the desire to obtain good repute in this world and high ranks in the Hereafter. As for its conditions: that the testator be eligible for donation, that he not be in debt, that the legatee be alive at the time of the will even if not yet born, ... that the legatee be a stranger (non-heir), that he not be a killer, that the bequeathed thing be something capable of being owned by another through a contract during the testator's life, whether existing or non-existent, and that the bequeathed be within one-third ... In al-Nihaya, etc. ... As for its pillar: his saying 'I bequeath such-and-such'.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Wasaya (Book of Wills) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It begins by justifying the placement of this book near the end of the overall work, noting that death is the final stage of life. The author then outlines eight aspects of the discussion, though the text only covers definitions, cause, conditions, and pillar. The linguistic definition is supported by Quranic verses 5:106 and 4:12. The legal definition given in most commentaries is 'a transfer of ownership deferred until after death, by way of donation, whether in specific objects or benefits.' The author criticizes this for excluding rights of Allah and debts; he suggests including those as well. He then presents a refined definition from some later scholars: in language, it is requesting someone to do something after one's death; in Shari'ah, it is the same transfer but with emphasis on the second meaning (using 'ila'). The cause (sabab) is the desire for good reputation and heavenly reward. The conditions are listed from earlier sources: testator eligibility, no debt, legatee alive (or rather existing) at time of will, legatee is non-heir, legatee not a killer, bequeathed property is ownable, and bequest within one-third of estate. The author critiques each condition: the debt condition should specify that the debt is overwhelming the estate, not absolute; the legatee condition should be existence not life (since a fetus may be considered existing); and the one-third condition should be qualified by whether there are heirs and whether they consent. The pillar is simply the verbal expression 'I bequeath...' This is standard Hanafi fiqh, but the author (Ibn Nujaym) provides critical refinement typical of later fatwa works, stressing precision in wording and conditions.

Key Terms
وصية (waṣiyyah): A legal act of granting ownership or benefit deferred until after death, by way of donation.
تمليك مضاف لما بعد الموت (tamlīk muḍāf limā ba‘d al-mawt): Transfer of ownership that is suspended (muḍāf) until after the death of the testator, i.e., the ownership vests in the legatee only after death.
إيصاء (īṣā’): Linguistically, requesting someone to do something after one's death; used with 'ila' for the specific meaning of deferred ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the cause (sabab) for the legislation of wills?
A) To ensure the testator's wealth is distributed according to Quranic shares.
B) The desire for good repute in this world and high ranks in the Hereafter.
C) To prevent disputes among heirs after death.
D) It is an obligation upon every Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of wasiyya is a deferred transfer of ownership by donation, but it must be understood broadly to include rights and debts.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate

Conditions and Pillar of a Valid Will
Lists and critiques the conditions for a valid will, then states the pillar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven conditions for a valid will according to the Hanafi school and explain the author's refinements regarding the legatee's existence and the one-third limit.

Core Idea
A will is valid only if the legatee exists (not necessarily alive) and the bequest does not exceed one-third unless heirs consent.

This lesson continues the discussion of wills by focusing on the conditions (shurut) and pillar (rukn) as presented in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author critiques earlier summaries, refining the conditions for testator eligibility, absence of overwhelming debt, legatee existence, non-heir status, non-killer, ownable property, and bequest within one-third. He also emphasizes that the pillar is simply the testator's verbal expression.

Guided Path
1
List the conditions mentioned in al-Nihaya
The passage enumerates seven conditions: testator eligibility, no debt, legatee alive at will time, legatee non-heir, legatee not a killer, bequeathed property ownable, and bequest within one-third.
These are standard in Hanafi fiqh, but the authors will critique them.
2
Analyze each condition with the author's critique
For each condition, note the author's objection: (1) debt condition should be specific to overwhelming debt; (2) legatee condition should be 'existing' not 'alive'; (3) one-third condition must be qualified by presence of heirs and their consent.
The author uses the term 'مقيد' (qualified) and 'لا بد من التقييد'.
3
Understand the refined conditions
After critique, the correct conditions are: testator eligible for donation, no overwhelming debt, legatee existing at will time (including fetus if born within six months), non-heir, not a killer, bequeathed property ownable, and bequest within one-third unless no heirs or heirs consent.
This is the mufta bihi position as per later Hanafi scholarship.
4
Identify the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is simply the testator's expression, e.g., 'I bequeath such-and-such' (أوصيت بكذا).
Unlike conditions, the pillar is straightforward and undisputed.

الحسن في الدنيا ووصول الدرجات العالية في العقبي. وأما شرائطها فكون الموصي أهلاً للتبرع، وأن لا يكون مديوناً، وكون الموصى له حياً وقت الوصية وإن لم يكن مولوداً حتى إذا أوصى للجنين إذا كان موجوداً حياً للتمليك من الغير بعقد من العقود حال حياة الموصي، سواء كان موجوداً في الحال أو معدوماً. وأن يكون أيضاً الموصى به بقدر الثلث حتى إنها لا تصح فيما زاد على الثلث؛ في النهاية. وفي العناية أيضاً بطريق الإجمال. وفي الأصل ومن شروطها كون الموصي أهلاً للتبرع فلا تصح من صبي ولا عبد. وأقول : فيه قصور بلا خلل؛ أما أولاً فلأنه جعل من شرائطها أن لا يكون الموصي مديوناً بدون التقييد بأن يكون الدين مستغرقاً لتركته والشرط عدم هذا الدين المقيد لا عدم الدين المطلق كما صرح به في البدائع وغيره. وأما ثانياً فلأنه جعل من شرائطها كون الموصى له حياً وقت الوصية والشرط كونه موجوداً وقت الوصية لا كونه حياً ألا ترى إطلاقه فإن الموصي إذا ترك ورثه فإنما لا تصح وصيته بما زاد على الثلث إن لم تجز الورثة، وإن أجازوه صحت وصیته به. وأما إذا لم يترك وارثاً فتصح وصيته بما زاد على الثلث حتى بجميع ماله عندنا كما تقرر في موضعه فلا بد من التقييد مرتين مرة بأن يكون له وارث، وأخرى بأن لا يجيزه الوارث والله أعلم. وأما ركنها فقوله أوصيت بكذا.
Book of Wills. The will is a transfer of ownership deferred until after death. ... The scholars said: Placing the Book of Wills at the end of the book is apparently appropriate since the last condition of a human in this world is death, and the will is a transaction at the time of death. I say: It is objected that the Book of Wills is not placed at the end of this book; rather, what is placed at the end is the Book of the Hermaphrodite, as you see. Yes, many authors have placed it at the end of their books, but the discussion is about the commentary of this book. A response can be given from the commentators: they meant 'end' in a relative sense. ... The discussion about the will is from eight aspects: first, its linguistic interpretation; second, its legal interpretation; third, the reason for its legislation; fourth, its pillar; fifth, its condition; sixth, its description; seventh, its ruling; eighth, the proof of its legitimacy. As for the will linguistically, it is a noun meaning the verbal noun 'tawsiyah', and from it is the saying of Allah: 'at the time of the will' [5:106]. Then the bequeathed thing is called a will, and from it is His saying: 'after a will you make' [4:12]. In Shari'ah, the will is a transfer of ownership deferred until after death by way of donation, whether in specific objects or benefits; thus in all commentaries. I say: This definition is not comprehensive because it does not include the rights of Allah and the debt owed by the testator. ... The cause of the will is the cause of all donations, which is the desire to obtain good repute in this world and high ranks in the Hereafter. As for its conditions: that the testator be eligible for donation, that he not be in debt, that the legatee be alive at the time of the will even if not yet born, ... that the legatee be a stranger (non-heir), that he not be a killer, that the bequeathed thing be something capable of being owned by another through a contract during the testator's life, whether existing or non-existent, and that the bequeathed be within one-third ... In al-Nihaya, etc. ... As for its pillar: his saying 'I bequeath such-and-such'.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Wasaya (Book of Wills) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It begins by justifying the placement of this book near the end of the overall work, noting that death is the final stage of life. The author then outlines eight aspects of the discussion, though the text only covers definitions, cause, conditions, and pillar. The linguistic definition is supported by Quranic verses 5:106 and 4:12. The legal definition given in most commentaries is 'a transfer of ownership deferred until after death, by way of donation, whether in specific objects or benefits.' The author criticizes this for excluding rights of Allah and debts; he suggests including those as well. He then presents a refined definition from some later scholars: in language, it is requesting someone to do something after one's death; in Shari'ah, it is the same transfer but with emphasis on the second meaning (using 'ila'). The cause (sabab) is the desire for good reputation and heavenly reward. The conditions are listed from earlier sources: testator eligibility, no debt, legatee alive (or rather existing) at time of will, legatee is non-heir, legatee not a killer, bequeathed property is ownable, and bequest within one-third of estate. The author critiques each condition: the debt condition should specify that the debt is overwhelming the estate, not absolute; the legatee condition should be existence not life (since a fetus may be considered existing); and the one-third condition should be qualified by whether there are heirs and whether they consent. The pillar is simply the verbal expression 'I bequeath...' This is standard Hanafi fiqh, but the author (Ibn Nujaym) provides critical refinement typical of later fatwa works, stressing precision in wording and conditions.

Key Terms
شرائط الوصية (shurāṭ al-waṣiyyah): The conditions that must be fulfilled for the will to be valid, including testator eligibility, legatee existence, and bequest within one-third.
مستغرق للتركة (mustaghriq li-l-tarika): Debt that exceeds the entire estate, making the testator effectively insolvent.
ركن الوصية (rukn al-waṣiyyah): The pillar of the will: the testator's verbal expression signifying the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's refined condition, what is the correct criterion for the legatee at the time of the will?
A) The legatee must be alive.
B) The legatee must be existing.
C) The legatee must be at least six months old.
D) The legatee must be born.

Key Takeaway
A valid Hanafi will requires the legatee to exist at the time of the will and the bequest to not exceed one-third unless heirs consent or none exist.

The One-Third Limit: Validity vs. Execution in Bequests
Ruling on maximum bequest with hadith evidence and terminological refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests exceeding one-third and explain why the wording 'لا تصح' is preferred over 'لا تجوز'.

Core Idea
A bequest exceeding one-third is not executed without heir consent — 'invalid' means non-execution, not voidness.

This lesson examines the one-third rule for bequests to non-heirs, supported by the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas. The commentary refines the legal terminology: 'لا تصح' (not valid) is preferred over 'لا تجوز' (not permissible) because lack of validity implies lack of permissibility, but the reverse does not hold. The intended meaning is non-execution (la yanfudh) until the heirs consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on bequests to non-heirs
The text states that a bequest to a non-heir (ajnabi) is valid for one-third without heir consent, but not valid for any excess.
The ruling is based on the Prophet's instruction to Sa'd: one-third is the maximum.
2
Examine the primary evidence (dalil)
The hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas is cited: the Prophet forbade bequeathing more than one-third, indicating the limit.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning, so its thubut is qati'.
3
Analyse the terminology: 'لا تصح' vs 'لا تجوز'
The author prefers 'لا تصح' (not valid) over al-Hidayah's 'لا تجوز' (not permissible). The key distinction: lack of validity necessarily implies lack of permissibility, but not vice versa. 'لا تصح' clearly indicates non-execution.
The phrase means the bequest does not take effect (nafadh) until the heirs consent.
4
Apply the multiple-will analogy
If someone bequeaths two-thirds, it is treated as two separate bequests: one valid for one-third, and the other suspended for the excess. This is why 'لا تصح' applies only to the excess, not the entire bequest.
This resolves the apparent contradiction: the wording is used for part of the meaning (excess) but not the whole.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تصح الوصية للأجنبي بالثلث من غير إجازة الوارث ولا تجوز بما زاد على الثلث لما روي عن سعد بن أبي وقاص أنه قال: جاءني رسول الله صلى اشتد عليه وسلم يعودني من وجع قلت : يا رسول الله قد بلغ بي من الوجع ما ترى وأنا بي ذو مال ولا يرثني إلا ابنة لي افأتصدق بثلثي مالي؟ قال: لا. قال قلت: فالشطر يا رسول الله؟ قال: لا. قال قلت : فالثلث؟ قال : فالثلث والثلث كثير إنك إن تذر ورثتك أغنياء خير من إن تذرهم عالة يتكففون الناس ولأن حق الورثة تعلق بماله لانعقاد إليهم وهو استغناؤه عن المال إلا أن الشرع لم يظهر في حق الأجانب بقدر الثلث ليتدارك تقصيره وأظهره في حق الورثة لأن الظاهر أنه لا يتصدق به عليهم تحرزاً عما يتفق لهم من التأذي بالايثار، وقد جاء في الحديث أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال «الحيف في الوصية من أكبر الكبائر وفسروه بالزيادة على الثلث وبالوصية للوارث. قال رحمه الله : (ولا تصح بما زاد على الثلث فهذه العبارة أولى من عبارة الهداية حيث قال : ولا تجوز لأنه يلزم من عدم الصحة عدم الجواز ولا يلزم من عدم الجواز عدم الصحة، والمراد بعدم الصحة عدم النفاذ حتى ينفذ بل يتوقف على الإجازة كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. قال بعض المتأخرين : يعني لا يجوز بما زاد على الثلث حتى لا يجوز في حق الفاضل على الثلث بل في حق الثلث، فقط لا أنه لا تجوز هذه الوصية أصلاً. فإن قلت: كيف جاز استعمال اللفظ في بعض مدلولاته دون بعض وبأي وجه أمكن ذلك؟ قلت: يجعله في حكم وصايا متعددة بأن يجعل قوله أوصيت لفلان بثلثي مالي في قوة قوله أوصيت له بثلثه دون الزائد والوصية تارة تكون منجزة وتارة معلقة بشرط فيجب أن يعلم بأن تعلق الوصية بالشرط جائز.
Then the will for a stranger is valid for one-third without the permission of the heir, and it is not valid for what exceeds one-third, because of what is narrated from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas that he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, came to visit me due to an illness. I said: O Messenger of Allah, the illness has reached me as you see, and I have wealth and only a daughter inherits from me, so should I give in charity two-thirds of my wealth? He said: No. I said: Half, O Messenger of Allah? He said: No. I said: One-third? He said: One-third, and one-third is much. Indeed, if you leave your heirs rich, it is better than leaving them poor, begging from people. And because the right of the heirs is attached to his property due to their connection to him, and his need for the wealth is over, except that the law did not manifest it with respect to strangers to the extent of one-third so that he can make up for his deficiency, and it manifested it with respect to the heirs because it is apparent that he does not give charity to them out of caution against the harm that may befall them from being preferred over others. And it has come in the hadith that he, peace be upon him, said: 'Injustice in the will is among the major sins,' and they interpreted it as exceeding one-third and bequeathing to an heir. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is not valid for what exceeds one-third) so this expression is better than the expression of al-Hidayah where he said: 'and it is not permissible' because from lack of validity follows lack of permissibility, but from lack of permissibility does not necessarily follow lack of validity. And what is meant by lack of validity is lack of execution, so it does not execute but rather depends on permission, as will come, Allah willing. Some later scholars said: It means it is not permissible for what exceeds one-third, so it is not permissible with respect to the excess over one-third, but only with respect to one-third, not that this will is not permissible at all. If you say: How is it permissible to use the word for some of its meanings and not others, and in what way is that possible? I say: It makes it in the ruling of multiple wills by making his statement 'I bequeath to so-and-so two-thirds of my wealth' equivalent to his statement 'I bequeath to him one-third of it' without the excess. And the will is sometimes executed immediately and sometimes conditional upon a condition, so it must be known that attaching the will to a condition is permissible.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that a bequest to a non-heir is valid only up to one-third of the estate without the consent of the heirs. The hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas is cited as the primary evidence: the Prophet forbade bequeathing more than one-third, stating 'one-third is much.' The commentary then clarifies the wording used in the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'لا تصح' (not valid) is preferred over 'لا تجوز' (not permissible) used in al-Hidayah, because lack of validity implies lack of permissibility, but the converse is not true. The intended meaning is that the bequest does not execute (non-execution) until the heirs consent. It does not mean the bequest itself is void; rather, it is suspended. Later scholars explain that 'لا تجوز' means it is not permissible for the excess, but the bequest is still valid for one-third. The passage uses the analogy of multiple wills: saying 'I bequeath two-thirds' is treated as two separate bequests: one valid for one-third and the other suspended for the remaining.

Key Terms
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum bequest to a non-heir without heir consent.
لا تصح (la tasihh): Does not execute; the bequest is valid in essence but its effect is suspended pending heir consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the expression 'لا تصح' preferred over 'لا تجوز'?
A) Because 'لا تجوز' is incorrect Arabic.
B) Because lack of validity implies lack of permissibility, but not vice versa.
C) Because 'لا تجوز' applies only to the excess, while 'لا تصح' applies to the entire bequest.
D) Because the author of al-Hidayah made a mistake.

Key Takeaway
A bequest exceeding one-third is not void but suspended; the Hanafi phrasing 'لا تصح' precisely conveys non-execution until heirs consent.

Best Practices in Making a Will Based on Wealth and Priorities
Recommendations on when and for whom to bequeath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommendation regarding making a will based on the testator's wealth and identify the priority order for beneficiaries.

Core Idea
The best will is made by a wealthy testator, prioritizing obligatory dues, then relatives, then neighbors.

This passage provides practical guidance for a testator on when and for whom to make a will. It distinguishes between those with little wealth and those with much, giving different recommendations. It also sets a priority list for bequests: first any obligatory duties, then relatives, then neighbors. Understanding these nuances helps avoid unintended neglect of heirs or overburdening the estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testator's wealth category
Determine if the testator has 'little wealth' or 'much wealth' as defined by the school. The text gives two measures: leaving each heir at least 4,000 dirhams (Abu Hanifa) or 10,000 (al-Fadl). This affects the recommendation.
The term 'little' and 'much' are relative; the school provides practical thresholds.
2
State the recommended action
For a person with little wealth, the best is not to bequeath anything (makruh tanzihi to bequeath). For a person with much wealth, the best is to bequeath without disobedience (mandub).
The recommendation is based on preserving heirs' share and avoiding sin.
3
Apply the priority order for beneficiaries
The testator should first fulfill any obligatory acts (e.g., unpaid zakat, debts), then bequeath to relatives, and if relatives are rich, to neighbors.
This order reflects the Hanafi principle of starting with duties, then family, then community.
4
Distinguish between hukm and advice
These are recommendations (afdal), not obligatory rulings. The will itself is sunnah muakkadah for a wealthy person, but the specific advice here is about the content and timing.
Al-afdal indicates a recommended practice that may change with circumstances.

وقوله «مستحبة الخ» الأفضل لمن كان قليل المال أن لا يوصي بشيء، والأفضل لمن كان له مال كثير أن بما لا معصية فيه. وقدر الأغنياء عند الإمام إذا ترك لكل واحد من الورثة أربعة آلاف دون الوصية، وعن الإمام الفضل عشرة آلاف وفي الموصي الذي أراد أن يوصي ينبغي أن يبدأ بالواجبات فإن لم يكن عليه شيء من الواجبات بدأ بالقرابة فإن كانوا أغنياء فالجيران . وفي الفتاوى : عامل السلطان أوصى بأن يعطي للفقراء كذا كذا من ماله قال أبو القاسم: إن علم بأنه مال غيره لا يحل أخذه وإن علم أنه مختلط بمال غيره جاز أخذه، وإن لم يعلم لا يجوز حتى يتبين أنه ماله قال الفقيه أبو الليث الجواز قول أبي حنيفة لأنه ملكه بالخلط، وعلى قولهما لا يجوز. وفي الخانية : إذا أوصى أن ينفق على فرس فلان جاز وهي وصية لصاحب الفرس . قال رحمه الله : (ولا تصح بما زاد على الثلث فهذه العبارة أولى من عبارة الهداية حيث قال : ولا تجوز لأنه يلزم من عدم الصحة عدم الجواز ولا يلزم من عدم الجواز والمراد بعدم الصحة عدم النفاذ حتى ينفذ بل يتوقف على الإجازة كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. قال بعض المتأخرين : يعني لا يجوز بما زاد على الثلث حتى لا يجوز في حق الفاضل على الثلث بل في حق الثلث، فقط لا أنه لا تجوز هذه الوصية أصلاً. فإن قلت: كيف جاز استعمال اللفظ في بعض مدلولاته دون بعض وبأي وجه أمكن ذلك؟ قلت: يجعله في حكم وصايا متعددة بأن يجعل قوله أوصيت لفلان بثلثي مالي في قوة قوله أوصيت له بثلثه دون الزائد والوصية تارة تكون منجزة وتارة معلقة بشرط فيجب أن يعلم بأن تعلق الوصية بالشرط جائز. وفي نوادر بشر عن أبي يوسف في الإملاء : إذا أوصى بثلثه لرجل على أن يحج عنه فهذا جائز إن قبل ذلك الموصى له ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال في وصيته ينفق على فلان كذا والموصى له غائب أو مات الموصي وهو غائب فهو بمنزلة رد الوصية ولا شيء له، وكذلك إن قدم فلم يقبل، وإن قدم وقبل فله ما مضى. قال أبو يوسف : أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وقال أن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له الأول أو لم يأب فالثلث للأول ولو أبي كان للآخر، لو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان فإن لم يشأ ذلك فلفلان فهو مثل الأول، ولو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان إن شاء وإن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له قبل أن يتكلم بشيء فالثلث مردود على الورثة. ابن سماعة عن محمد: رجل أوصى لرجل بوصية
And his statement 'recommended etc.': The best for one who has little wealth is not to bequeath anything, and the best for one who has much wealth is to bequeath without disobedience. The measure of the rich according to Imam Abu Hanifa is if he leaves for each of the heirs four thousand (dirhams) without the bequest, and according to Imam al-Fadl ten thousand. And for the testator who wants to bequeath, it is appropriate to start with the obligatory (acts). If he has no obligatory things, he starts with the relatives; if they are rich, then the neighbors. In al-Fatawa: An agent of the sultan bequeathed to give to the poor such-and-such from his wealth. Abu al-Qasim said: If he knows that it is someone else's wealth, it is not permissible to take it; if he knows that it is mixed with someone else's wealth, it is permissible to take it; and if he does not know, it is not permissible until it becomes clear that it is his wealth. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth (said): The permissibility is the statement of Abu Hanifa because he owns it by mixing, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not permissible. In al-Khaniyya: If he bequeaths that it be spent on so-and-so's horse, it is permissible, and it is a bequest for the owner of the horse. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is not valid for what exceeds one-third) so this expression is better than the expression of al-Hidayah where he said: 'and it is not permissible' because from lack of validity follows lack of permissibility, but from lack of permissibility does not necessarily follow lack of validity. And what is meant by lack of validity is lack of execution, so it does not execute but rather depends on permission, as will come, Allah willing. Some later scholars said: It means it is not permissible for what exceeds one-third, so it is not permissible with respect to the excess over one-third, but only with respect to one-third, not that this will is not permissible at all. If you say: How is it permissible to use the word for some of its meanings and not others, and in what way is that possible? I say: It makes it in the ruling of multiple wills by making his statement 'I bequeath to so-and-so two-thirds of my wealth' equivalent to his statement 'I bequeath to him one-third of it' without the excess. And the will is sometimes executed immediately and sometimes conditional upon a condition, so it must be known that attaching the will to a condition is permissible. In Nawadir of Bishr from Abu Yusuf in al-Imla': If he bequeaths his one-third to a man on condition that he perform Hajj on his behalf, this is permissible if the legatee accepts it. Ibn Samāʿa from Abu Yusuf: If he says in his will: 'Spend on so-and-so such-and-such' and the legatee is absent or the testator dies while he is absent, it is like the rejection of the bequest and he gets nothing. Similarly, if he comes and does not accept, and if he comes and accepts, he gets what has passed. Abu Yusuf said: He bequeathed one-third of his wealth to a man and said: 'If he refuses, it is for so-and-so.' If the first legatee dies or does not refuse, the one-third is for the first. If he refuses, it is for the other. If he said: 'One-third of my wealth is a bequest for so-and-so; if he does not want it, then for so-and-so,' it is like the first. If he said: 'One-third of my wealth is a bequest for so-and-so; if he wishes and if he refuses, it is for so-and-so,' and the legatee dies before saying anything, the one-third is returned to the heirs. Ibn Samāʿa from Muhammad: A man bequeathed to a man a bequest...
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage contains several subsidiary rulings. First, it gives practical advice: one with little wealth should not bequeath anything, while one with much wealth should bequeath without sin. The measure of being 'rich' according to Imam Abu Hanifa is leaving each heir at least 4,000 dirhams, and according to Imam al-Fadl, 10,000 dirhams. The testator should prioritize obligatory acts, then relatives, then neighbors. Next, a fatwa about a government agent: if his wealth is mixed with others, Abu Hanifa permits taking from it due to mixing, but the two disciples disagree. Another ruling: a bequest to spend on someone's horse is valid and considered a bequest to the horse's owner. Then there is a discussion about conditional bequests and cases where a legatee is absent. Several rulings from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad are cited regarding conditional appointments, including when a legatee dies before acceptance, the share goes back to the heirs. The passage ends with an incomplete fatwa from Ibn Samāʿa from Muhammad.

Key Terms
الأفضل (al-afdal): The best practice; in this context, the recommended course of action for the testator based on circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is better to make a will for all his wealth.
B) It is better to not make a will.
C) It is better to make a will for the poor.
D) It is better to make a will for his relatives.

Key Takeaway
The best will is made by a wealthy testator, prioritizing obligatory dues, then relatives if poor, then neighbors.

Fatawa on Mixed Wealth and Conditional Bequests
Fatawa on mixing and conditional bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on mixing (khalṭ) to determine ownership and explain the validity of conditional bequests and the effect of acceptance or rejection by the legatee.

Core Idea
Mixing property without distinguishing marks gives ownership to the mixer in Abu Hanifa's view; conditional bequests are valid subject to acceptance, and a legatee's death before acceptance voids the bequest.

This passage presents several fatwa cases: one about a government agent whose wealth is mixed with others', and several about conditional bequests where the legatee is absent, accepts, or rejects. Understanding these rulings helps a mufti handle complex modern scenarios involving commingled assets and conditional gifts.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the mixing (khalṭ) dispute
Identify the case: a sultan's agent bequeaths from his wealth which is mixed with others'. Abu Hanifa holds that mixing with no distinguishing marks transfers ownership to the mixer, so the bequest is valid. The two disciples disagree.
The principle: 'al-khalt yufīd al-milk' is specific to certain Hanafi rulings.
2
Determine the ruling on bequest to spend on a horse
If someone bequeaths that money be spent on a specific horse, it is valid and considered a bequest to the owner of the horse.
This is because the benefit accrues to the owner.
3
Differentiate between validity and permissibility
The author clarifies that 'la tasihh' (not valid) means 'not executable without permission', not that the will is void. This is a technical distinction.
The distinction between 'sihha' (validity) and 'nufadh' (execution) is crucial in Hanafi law.
4
Apply the rules for conditional bequests
Scenarios: if a legatee is absent and dies, it is like rejection; the bequest reverts. If he comes and accepts, he gets what has passed. If a bequest is conditional on acceptance/rejection, the condition determines the outcome.
Acceptance is required for the legatee to own the bequest.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Conditional Bequest Upon Recipient's Refusal
Ruling on conditional bequest transfer to second legatee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest conditional upon the first legatee's refusal or death before acceptance, and identify the conditions that trigger the transfer to the second legatee.

Core Idea
A conditional bequest transfers completely to the second if the first refuses or dies unaware.

Testators often wish to provide for alternative recipients if the primary legatee cannot or will not accept. The Hanafi school addresses this with a clear rule: when the testator explicitly conditions the bequest on the first legatee's refusal or death before acceptance, the entire bequest shifts to the named second legatee. This lesson unpacks the scenarios and the legal reasoning behind the transfer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional bequest
Recognize that the testator's statement creates a conditional transfer: the bequest is given to a first legatee, but if that legatee refuses or does not accept, it goes to a second legatee.
The wording is key—e.g., 'If so-and-so does not accept' or 'If so-and-so rejects'.
2
Determine the trigger event
Two triggers cause the bequest to pass to the second: (1) the first legatee is alive at the testator's death and refuses the bequest, or (2) the first legatee died before the testator without ever learning of the bequest.
Refusal means explicit rejection after the testator's death; death before knowledge is treated like refusal because the legatee never had a chance to accept.
3
Apply the consequence
In both cases, the entire bequest goes wholly to the second legatee. The first legatee's heirs have no claim, and the bequest is not split.
The second legatee takes the full amount, subject to the standard limit of one-third of the estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال إن لم يقبل فلان ما أوصيت له به أو قال إن رد فلان ما أوصيت به فهو لفلان فإذا الموصى له الأول حياً أو كان حياً فمات قبل الموصي ولم يعلم بالوصية قال هي للثاني كلها
And if he says: If so-and-so does not accept what I have bequeathed to him, or says: If so-and-so rejects what I have bequeathed to him, then it is for so-and-so. And if the first legatee is alive, or was alive and died before the testator without knowing of the bequest, he said: It is all for the second.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a conditional bequest. The testator makes a bequest to a first person (al-mūṣā lahu al-awwal) but stipulates that if that first person does not accept or rejects it, then the bequest goes to a second person. The ruling addresses two scenarios: (1) the first legatee is alive at the testator's death but refuses the bequest; (2) the first legatee was alive but died before the testator without ever learning of the bequest. In both cases, the entire bequest transfers to the second legatee. This is based on the principle that the bequest vests upon the testator's death, but if the legatee's right is nullified by refusal or death before acceptance, the conditional substitute takes effect fully. The ruling does not require the second legatee to give anything to the first's heirs.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A testamentary bequest of up to one-third of the estate to a non-heir, effective after death.
موصى له (mūṣā lahu): The legatee/recipient of the bequest.
رد (radd): Rejection of the bequest by the legatee, which nullifies his right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says, 'If Zaid does not accept my bequest, then it is for Bakr,' and Zaid is alive at the testator's death but refuses, what happens?
A) The bequest is void.
B) The bequest goes to Zaid's heirs.
C) The entire bequest goes to Bakr.
D) The bequest is split between Zaid and Bakr.

Key Takeaway
A conditional bequest where the first legatee refuses or dies without knowledge passes entirely to the named second legatee.

Conditional Bequest with Debt Payment: Cases of Validity
Ruling on bequest with condition to pay debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for a bequest conditioned on paying the testator's debt, distinguishing valid and invalid cases based on knowledge of debt and one-third, and the presence of ribawi items.

Core Idea
A bequest conditioned on paying the testator's debt is valid only if both are known and no ribawi excess exists.

This lesson examines a specific type of conditional bequest (wasiyyah bi-shart qada' al-dayn) reported from Abu Yusuf. The testator gives one-third of his estate to a legatee on condition that the legatee pays the testator's debt. The validity hinges on whether the debt and the one-third are known (ma'lum) or unknown (majhul), and on the composition of the one-third, especially the presence of gold or silver (ribawi items). Understanding these conditions prevents gharar (uncertainty) and riba in bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the variables
Determine whether the debt is known or unknown, and whether the one-third is known or unknown. Also note if the one-third contains gold/silver (dirhams).
2
Apply the first filter
If either the debt or the one-third is unknown (majhul), the bequest is void (batil) due to gharar.
Uncertainty in the subject matter invalidates the bequest.
3
Check for ribawi items
If both are known and the one-third contains no gold or silver, the bequest is valid (ja'iz). The legatee must pay the debt to receive the one-third, analogous to a sale.
4
Evaluate if dirhams are present
If the one-third contains dirhams (silver currency), compare the amount of dirhams to the debt. If the dirhams exceed the debt, the bequest is void due to riba al-fadl (excess in exchange of same genus). If dirhams are less than or equal to the debt, it is permissible.
Immediate possession and payment at death requires proportional reduction of dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن أبي يوسف : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وشرط عليه أن يقضي دينه معناه شرط الموصي على الموصى له أن يقضي دين الموصي فهذا على وجوه : إن كان الدين مجهولاً أو كان معلوماً إلا أن الثلث مجهول فالوصية باطلة وإن كان الدين معلوماً والثلث معلوماً فإن لم يكن في الثلث ذهب ولا فضة فهو جائز ويجب له الثلث بالدين إذا قبل كما يجب في البيع، وإن كان في الثلث دراهم إن كان أكثر من الدين فإن هذا لا يجوز من قبيل أن هذا دراهم بدراهم وفضل عروض سوى ذلك، وإن كانت الدراهم التي في الثلث أقل من الدين جاز، فإن قبض الثلث ساعة يموت أو قبض الدراهم التي في الثلث ساعة يموت وقضى الدين ساعته انتقص ذلك في الدراهم ما يخصه وجاز في العروض.
From Abu Yusuf: A man bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and stipulates that he pay his debt. Its meaning is that the testator stipulates on the legatee to pay the testator's debt. So this has aspects: If the debt is unknown or if it is known but the one-third is unknown, the bequest is void. If the debt is known and the one-third is known, and there is no gold or silver in the one-third, it is permissible and the one-third becomes owed to him for the debt if he accepts, as it is owed in a sale. If there are dirhams in the one-third and they are more than the debt, this is not permissible because it is dirhams for dirhams with an excess along with other goods. If the dirhams in the one-third are less than the debt, it is permissible. If he takes possession of the one-third at the time of death or takes possession of the dirhams in the one-third at the time of death and pays the debt immediately, that reduces from the dirhams what pertains to him, and it is permissible in the goods.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from Abu Yusuf details a complex bequest where the testator gives one-third of his estate to a legatee on condition that the legatee pays the testator's debt. The ruling is categorized into several cases. First, if the debt is unknown (majhūl) or the one-third is unknown, the bequest is void due to uncertainty (gharar). Second, if both are known and the one-third contains no gold or silver (i.e., no ribawi items), the bequest is valid and the legatee must pay the debt to receive the one-third, analogous to a sale. Third, if the one-third contains dirhams (silver currency) and their value exceeds the debt, it is invalid because it involves a sale of dirhams for dirhams with an excess (ribā al-fadl) along with other goods. Fourth, if the dirhams are less than the debt, it is permissible. If the legatee takes possession immediately at death and pays the debt, the dirham amount is reduced proportionally, and the rest (goods) is valid. This shows the Hanafi concern for avoiding ribā and gharar in conditional bequests.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): A debt owed by the testator, which becomes a liability on the estate.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the testator's estate, the maximum that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without consent.
ربا (ribā): Usury or interest; here pertaining to ribā al-fadl in the exchange of dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, a bequest of one-third conditioned on paying the testator's debt is void when:
A) The debt is known and the one-third is known, and there is no gold or silver in the one-third.
B) The debt is unknown or the one-third is unknown.
C) The dirhams in the one-third are less than the debt.
D) The legatee takes immediate possession and pays the debt.

Key Takeaway
A bequest conditioned on paying the testator's debt requires both the debt and the one-third to be known, and if dirhams are present, they must not exceed the debt to avoid riba.

Conditional Manumission in Wills: Non-Marriage Condition
Ruling on conditional manumission by will with a non-marriage condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of freedom conditioned on not marrying, and explain the effects of the condition being fulfilled and later violated.

Core Idea
A bequest to free a slave on condition of not marrying is valid; later marriage does not revoke freedom or create liability.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a specific scenario: a master bequeaths that his female slave be freed on condition that she does not marry. After the master's death, she declares she will not marry. According to the Hanafi school, she is freed provided the bequest is within one-third of the estate. Importantly, if she later marries, her marriage is valid, her freedom stands, and she owes no compensation to the heirs. The three founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) agree on this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
The act is a bequest (wasiyya) of manumission (itq) with a condition (shart) that the slave does not marry. Note whether the condition is time-bound (e.g., 'for a day') or absolute (e.g., 'never').
The text mentions both variants: if the condition is time-bound ('if she does not marry for a day') or absolute ('on condition that she does not marry').
2
Determine when the condition is fulfilled
The condition is fulfilled by the slave's declaration after the master's death that she will not marry. This triggers the freedom if the bequest is valid (within one-third of the estate).
The declaration is sufficient; actual abstention is presumed.
3
Identify the consequence of later marriage
If she later marries, the marriage is valid, and her freedom and bequest remain valid. She is not required to work (sa'y) to compensate the heirs.
This is true regardless of whether the condition was time-bound or absolute, according to the Hanafi school.
4
Note the unanimous Hanafi position
The ruling is attributed to 'our three scholars' (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani), indicating complete intra-madhhab agreement.
Other schools may differ, but within the Hanafi school, this is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أعتقوه إن لم يتزوج شهراً. فإن علق عتقه بالثبات على فعل غير مؤقت حال حياته بأن قال المملوكه حال حياته إن ثبت مع ولدي أو في هذه الدار شهراً فأنت حرة فثبتت ساعة عتقت، وكذا إذا علق عتقه بالثبات على فعل غير مؤقت بأن أوصى بأن يعتقوها على أن لا تتزوج أو قال إن لم تتزوج إذا قالت بعد موت المولى لا أتزوج فإنها تعتق إذا كانت تخرج من ثلث ماله ؛ هكذا وقع في بعض النسخ. وفي بعض النسخ إذا لم تتزوج يوماً أو أقل وأكثر فإن الوصية لها صحيحة، فإن تزوجت بعد ذلك صح نكاحها ولا يبطل عتقها ووصيتها ولا يلزمها السعاية في شيء للورثة وهذا قول علمائنا الثلاثة
He said: Free them if he does not marry for a month. If he attaches his freedom to persisting in a non-time-bound action during his lifetime – such that he said to his female slave during his lifetime: 'If you stay with my child or in this house for a month, you are free' – and she stays for an hour, she is freed. Likewise, if he attaches his freedom to persisting in a non-time-bound action by bequeathing that they free her on condition that she does not marry, or says 'If she does not marry' – if she says after the master's death 'I will not marry,' then she is freed if it comes out of his third. This is how it occurs in some copies. In some copies: 'If she does not marry for a day or less or more, the bequest for her is valid. If she marries after that, her marriage is valid, and her freedom and bequest are not invalidated, and she is not obliged to work (sa'y) for anything for the heirs.' This is the statement of our three scholars.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This is a ruling on conditional manumission in a will. The author discusses a scenario where a master stipulates a condition for freedom, such as staying in a place for a month or not marrying. If the condition is non-time-bound (like not marrying ever), and the slave declares after the master's death that she will not marry, she is freed provided the bequest is within one-third of the estate. There is a variant that if the bequest is absolute as to time, marriage afterward does not nullify freedom or the bequest, and she does not have to compensate the heirs through work. This is the unanimous position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms
عتق (itq): Manumission, freeing a slave.
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest or will.
سعاية (sa'y): Working for the heirs to pay off a debt or compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a testator bequeaths freedom to his slave on condition that she does not marry, and she declares after his death that she will not marry, what is the effect if she later marries?
A) Her freedom is revoked and she must pay the heirs.
B) Her marriage is invalid, and she remains free.
C) Her marriage is valid, and her freedom and bequest remain valid, with no obligation to the heirs.
D) Her freedom is valid only if she never marries; marriage revokes it.

Key Takeaway
A conditional bequest of freedom on not marrying is valid once the condition is fulfilled; later marriage does not affect the vested freedom.

Conditional Bequests to an Umm Walad
Ruling on conditional bequests to an umm walad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for a bequest to an umm walad conditional on marriage or staying with her child, and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A bequest conditional on not marrying is binding; time-bound conditions invalidate the bequest if broken.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents several scenarios involving a bequest to an umm walad. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly executing such bequests and avoiding common misunderstandings about when a bequest is revoked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main conditions
The passage discusses two types of conditions: (1) marriage-related (open-ended or time-bound) and (2) staying with the child.
2
Distinguish open-ended vs time-bound conditions
An open-ended condition (e.g., 'if she does not marry') is fulfilled by a declaration of intent after the testator's death; subsequent marriage does not revoke. A time-bound condition (e.g., 'as long as she does not marry for a month') requires actual abstinence for the full period; marriage within the period invalidates.
The wording 'ما لم تتزوج شهراً' triggers a time-bound condition.
3
Analyze the consequence of marrying after fulfillment
If she declares she will not marry (open-ended) and receives the bequest, later marriage does not require restitution.
The bequest is irrevocable once earned.
4
Examine the condition of staying with the child
If the condition is to stay with her child, even a brief stay (one hour) suffices for her to earn the bequest.
The condition is considered fulfilled by minimal compliance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أوصى لأم ولده بألف على أن تتزوج أو قال إن لم تتزوج إن قالت لا أتزوج بعد موت الموصي فإنه يعطي لها وصيتها، فإن تزوجت بعد ذلك لا يسترد الألف منها ولو قال ما لم تتزوج شهراً فهو على ما قال لا تستحق وصيتها ما لم تترك التزوج شهراً، وإذا تزوجت قبل مضي الشهر تبطل وصيتها. أوصى لها بألف درهم على أن تثبت ولدها فمكثت مع ولدها ساعة استحقت مع الوصية .
He said: If he bequeaths to his umm walad a thousand on condition that she marries, or says 'if she does not marry,' then if she says after the testator's death 'I will not marry,' he gives her her bequest. If she marries after that, the thousand is not taken back from her. If he says 'as long as she does not marry for a month,' then it is as he said: she does not deserve her bequest unless she refrains from marrying for a month, and if she marries before the month passes, her bequest is invalidated. If he bequeaths to her a thousand dirhams on condition that she stays with her child, and she stays with her child for an hour, she deserves the bequest.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage details rulings on conditional bequests to an umm walad (a female slave who has borne her master's child). The conditions involve marriage or staying with her child. If the condition is open-ended (e.g., 'if she does not marry'), and she declares she will not marry after the master's death, she receives the bequest, and even if she later marries, it is not taken back. However, if the condition is time-bound (e.g., 'as long as she does not marry for a month'), she must refrain from marriage for that period. Marrying before the period ends invalidates the bequest. Additionally, if the bequest is conditioned on staying with her child, even a brief stay (one hour) suffices for her to deserve the bequest.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has given birth to her master's child.
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man bequeaths 1000 dirhams to his umm walad on condition that she does not marry for a month. She marries after 20 days. What is the ruling?
A) She receives the bequest because marriage does not invalidate it.
B) Her bequest is invalidated because she married before the month passed.
C) She receives half the amount.
D) The bequest is valid but she must repay the heirs.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to an umm walad conditional on not marrying is binding; marriage only revokes if the condition is time-bound and broken before the period ends.

Conditional Bequest: Servant Until Independence
Ruling on conditional bequest of a servant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a conditional bequest of a servant to serve children until independence, and distinguish the conditions based on the children's age.

Core Idea
The independence of the children determines when the servant is freed.

This lesson examines a specific conditional bequest: a testator leaves his maidservant to serve his children until they can manage without her, after which she is freed. The ruling hinges on whether the children are adults or minors at the time of the bequest. Understanding this distinction is crucial for drafting valid wills and fulfilling the testator's intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? A bequest of a maidservant with a condition. The ruling: the bequest is valid (sahih) and the condition must be fulfilled.
The condition is that the servant serves until the children become independent.
2
Distinguish the two cases
The passage splits the ruling into two: adult children vs. minor children. Identify the difference in how 'independence' is defined.
For adults, independence is marriage or ability to afford a servant. For minors, it is reaching puberty.
3
Apply the definition of independence for adults
For adult children: the daughter is served until she marries; the son until he marries or can buy a servant. Both conditions must be met for the servant to be freed.
The son's independence can be achieved either by marriage or by having means to hire a servant.
4
Apply the ruling for minors
For minor children: they are served until they reach puberty. At that point, they are considered independent and the servant is freed.
If a child dies before reaching puberty, the condition fails.
5
Determine the consequence of death before independence
If any child dies before becoming independent, the condition is not fulfilled. The servant is not freed and the bequest becomes void.
This applies to both adult and minor children.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : وإذا أوصى لرجل بخادمه على أن يقيم مع ابنته ومع ابنه حتى يستغنيا ثم هي حرة فهذا على وجهين : فإما كانا كبيرين أو كانا صغيرين فإن كانا كبيرين فإنها تخدم الابنة حتى تتزوج وتخدم الابن حتى يتأهل أو يجد ما يشتري به خادماً يخدمه فيستغني عن خدمتها، وإن كانا صغيرين تخدمهما حتى يبلغا وإن مات أحدهما أو ماتا جميعاً قبل أن يستغنيا فإن الجارية لا تعتق وتبطل الوصية .
He said: If he bequeaths to a man his maidservant on condition that she stay with his daughter and his son until they become independent, and then she is free. This is two cases: either they are adults or they are minors. If they are adults, she serves the daughter until she marries, and she serves the son until he gets married or finds something with which to buy a servant to serve him, so that he becomes independent of her service. If they are minors, she serves them until they reach puberty. If one of them dies or both die before becoming independent, then the maidservant is not freed and the bequest is invalid.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This ruling addresses a conditional bequest where a testator bequeaths a maidservant to be freed after serving his children until they no longer need her. The rule distinguishes between adult and minor children. Adult children: the daughter is served until marriage, the son until he marries or can afford a servant. Minor children: the service lasts until they reach puberty. If any child dies before reaching independence, the condition fails; the maidservant is not freed, and the bequest is void. This is a Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
خادمة (khadama): Maidservant.
استغناء (istighna'): Becoming independent, no longer needing service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man bequeaths his maidservant to serve his two adult children until they become independent, then she is free. The son gets married but the daughter does not. What happens to the maidservant?
A) She is freed immediately.
B) She continues to serve the daughter until she marries, then is freed.
C) The bequest is invalid because the daughter is not married.
D) She is freed after the son marries, regardless of the daughter.

Key Takeaway
The condition in a will must be fulfilled precisely; independence for adults is defined by marriage or ability to hire a servant, not by age.

Subsidiary Items in a Bequest: Offspring, Earnings, and Custom
Explaining what enters a bequest by way of subsidiary (taba') and the dispute among later scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the inclusion of subsidiary items arising after the testator's death but before acceptance, and apply the mufta bihi ruling from the later mashayikh.

Core Idea
In Hanafi wasiyyah, subsidiary items hinge on timing; acceptance relates back to death, creating grey areas resolved by custom.

A bequest can include more than the principal item—offspring of a bequeathed slave or earnings from property may also pass to the legatee. But when do these subsidiaries enter the bequest? The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq left this unaddressed, so the commentator clarifies Muhammad al-Shaybani's rulings and a subsequent dispute among later Hanafi scholars. This lesson unpacks the timing conditions and the reliance on 'urf (custom) to determine scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three timing scenarios
Muhammad gives two clear rulings: if offspring/earnings arise before testator's death → not in bequest; if after death but on the day of division/delivery → also not in bequest. A third scenario – after death but before acceptance – is left open, sparking a dispute.
The third scenario is the contested grey area.
2
Analyse the two Hanafi positions
Al-Quduri says such items are not part of the bequest, so they go to the legatee from the whole estate (not restricted to the third). The later mashayikh say they are part of the bequest, restricting them to the third. Both base their reasoning on when the bequest is finalised.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf; both rely on different interpretations of the time of transfer.
3
Apply the tarjih (preference) principle
The later scholars' view (mashayikh) is mufta bihi, as indicated by the author's presentation. In fatwa, one follows the view that the items are included and thus must come from the third.
The tarjih is based on later Hanafi methodology, not explicit text.
4
Examine the role of custom ('urf)
The Nawadir example: bequest of a wall includes its land; bequest of a date palm does not include land in old custom (where 'nakhla' meant a cut trunk), but in current custom it does. This shows that 'urf determines what is considered 'subsidiary'.
Custom can change the scope of bequest terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يتعرض المؤلف لبيان ما يدخل في الوصية بطريق التبع وما لا يدخل . قال محمد : الولد والكسب إذا ولدا قبل موت الموصي فإنهما لا يدخلان تحت الوصية . سواء كانا يخرجان من الثلث أو لا يخرجان فأما إذا حدث الولد والكسب بعد موت الموصي إن حدثا يوم القسمة والتسليم لا يدخلان تحت الوصية ولا يسلمان للموصى له بحكم الوصية حتى لا يعتبر فيها الثلث والثلثان، فأما إذا حدث الولد والكسب قبل قبول الموصى له قبل القسمة والتسليم هل يصير موصى به حتى يعتبر خروجه من الثلث أو لا يجعل موصى به لا يكون للموصى من غير اعتبار الثلث؟ لم يذكر محمد هذا في شيء من الكتب نصاً، وقد اختلف فيه المشايخ المتأخرون ؛ ذكر القدوري أنه لا يصير موصى به حتى لا يعتبر خروجه من الثلث وكان للموصى له من جميع المال كما لو حدث بعد القسمة والتسليم، ومشايخنا قالوا بأنه يصير موصى به حتى لا يعتبر خروجه من الثلث كما لو وجد قبل القبول. وفي نوادر ابراهيم عن محمد فيمن أوصى لرجل بحائط فهو بأرضه كله وصية، ولو أوصى بنخلة فهو على النخلة دون الأرض قال : إنما تسمى نخلة وهي مقطوعة وهذا في عرفهم، وفي عرفنا تسمى نخلة وهي قائمة أيضاً فعليه تدخل أرضها.
And the author did not address explaining what enters into the bequest by way of subsidiary and what does not. Muhammad said: The child and the earnings – if they come into existence before the testator's death, they are not included under the bequest, whether they come out of the third or not. As for if the child and earnings come into existence after the testator's death: if they occur on the day of division and delivery, they are not included under the bequest, and are not delivered to the legatee by virtue of the bequest, so that the third and two-thirds are not considered with respect to them. As for if the child and earnings come into existence before the legatee's acceptance, before division and delivery: does it become bequeathed so that its removal from the third is considered, or is it not considered bequeathed so that it is for the testator without consideration of the third? Muhammad did not mention this explicitly in any of the books. The later scholars differed: al-Quduri mentioned that it does not become bequeathed, so its removal from the third is not considered, and it is for the legatee from all the property as if it occurred after division and delivery. Our (later) scholars said that it does become bequeathed, so its removal from the third is considered, as if it existed before acceptance. And in Nawadir Ibrahim from Muhammad: regarding someone who bequeaths to a man a wall (ha'it), it is a bequest of the entire wall along with its land. If he bequeaths a date palm (nakhla), it is for the date palm only, without the land. He said: It is only called a 'date palm' when it is cut off. This is according to their custom. In our custom, it is called a 'date palm' even when standing, so its land is included.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage addresses what is included in a bequest by way of subsidiary (taba'). The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not cover this, so the commentator explains. Muhammad al-Shaybani's ruling: offspring (walad) and earnings (kash) that arise before the testator's death are not part of the bequest, regardless of whether they come from the third. If they arise after death on the day of division and delivery, they are also not included. The grey area is when they arise after death but before the legatee's acceptance. Muhammad did not address this explicitly, leading to a dispute among later Hanafi scholars: al-Quduri held they are not included (so the legatee takes them from the entire estate, not just the third), while the later mashayikh (e.g., from the Balkh school) held they are included and thus must come from the third. The passage then gives examples from Nawadir: a bequest of a wall (ha'it) includes the land; a bequest of a date palm (nakhla) does not include the land in the old custom where a palm tree meant a cut trunk, but in the current custom where a standing palm is called nakhla, the land is included. This shows the role of 'urf (custom) in determining the scope of a bequest.

Key Terms
ولد (walad): Offspring of a female slave bequeathed.
كسب (kash): Earnings or profits from the bequeathed property.
تبع (taba'): Subsidiary, what follows the principal item in a bequest.
عرف (urf): Custom, prevalent usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi scholars (المتأخرون), if a person bequeaths a female slave, and she gives birth before the legatee accepts the bequest but after the testator's death, what is the ruling on the child?
A) The child does not enter the bequest and is part of the estate for the heirs.
B) The child enters the bequest and must be from the testator's third.
C) The child enters the bequest and is given to the legatee without limitation.
D) The bequest is invalid because the child was born after death.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wasiyyah, subsidiary items arising after death but before acceptance are deemed part of the bequest per the later scholars, and custom defines the scope of ambiguous terms like 'date palm'.
