Bequest of a Palm Tree: Land and Root Included
Ruling on bequest of palm trees and vineyards

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what is included when a palm tree is bequeathed, including the distinction from a vineyard or garden.

Core Idea
A bequeathed standing palm tree includes its land; a vineyard includes only its root.

When someone bequeaths a specific item like a palm tree, the scope of what passes to the legatee depends on the wording and custom. This lesson explains the Hanafi position on palm trees and contrasts it with vineyards and gardens, based on narrations from Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequeathed item
Determine whether the bequest is for a palm tree (nakhla) or a vineyard/garden (karm/bustan). The ruling differs for each.
2
Check if the palm tree is standing
If the palm tree is standing (qā’ima), its land is included; if not, only the tree itself.
The text states 'if it is standing, its land is included'.
3
Contrast with vineyard/garden
For a vineyard or garden, the bequest includes the root (aṣl) but not the land, unlike a palm tree.
The author notes that the palm tree is not like a vineyard.
4
Apply the rule to gifts and sales
The same inclusion applies to gifts, charity, and sales: the donee/purchaser gets what is on the surface of the land (the tree).
Nawadir al-Mualla from Abu Yusuf extends the rule to other transfers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا للموصى عرفهم، وفي عرفنا تسمى نخلة وهي قائمة أيضاً فعليه تدخل أرضها. في نوادر المعلى عن أبي يوسف : أوصى لرجل نخل كثير أو نخلة واحدة أو وهب أو تصدق أو باع فله ما على ظهر الأرض، ولو أوصى له بكرم أو بستان أو جمة فله ذلك بأصله ولا يشبهه هذه النخلة، وذكر المعلى عن أبي يوسف : إذا أوصى بنخلة لإنسان ولآخر بثمرها فالوصية جائزة والنخل له بالنخل بأصله وأرضه وفي نوادر ابن سماعة عن محمد: إذا أوصى بزق زيت فهو على الزق دون الزيت ولو قال بزق الزيت فهو على الزق وحده، ولو بسفينة الطعام فهو على السفينة، وكذلك على هذه الوجوه في رواية الماء وقوصرة التمر. ولو أوصى لأحد بميزان فهو على العمود والكفتين والخيوط ولا يدخل فيه السنجات والغلاف، وهذا إذا كان بغير عينه، وأما إذا كان بعينه دخل فيه. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا أوصى لرجل بالميزان فله الكفتان والعمود ولا يمكن له السنجات، وأما القبان فهو له برمانته وكفته. وذكر الحسن بن زياد في كتاب الاختلاف عن أبي يوسف إذا أوصى لرجل بسيف فله النصل دون الجفن وهو قول أبي حنيفة. وعنه أن له السيف مع جفنه ورواية ابن سماعة موافقة لرواية الأصل. ولو أوصى بمصحف وله إذا أوصى غلاف فله المصحف دون الغلاف في قول أبي حنيفة . وفي البقالي له بقبة تركية فهو له بالآلة، فلو أوصى بحجلة فله الكسوة دون العيدان، وفيه أيضاً أبي يوسف : أوصى لرجل بسرج فكل شيء علق به وحرز فيه فهو له ولا يكون له غيره. وذكر الحسن في كتاب الاختلاف عن أبي يوسف في الوصية بالسرج أن له الدرفتين والركابين والمرة لا يكون للعبد والرفادة والصنقة. وذكر ابراهيم عن محمد في رجل مات فأعتق عبده قال : له كسوته ومنطقته . وإن قال متاعه يدخل فيه سيفه ومنطقته قال محمد هي وصية عبد الله بن المبارك لغلامه وفي نوارد بشر عن أبي يوسف أوصى لرجل بشاة من غنمه ولم يقل من غنمي هذه فأعطى الورثة الموصى له شاة قد ولدت بعد موت الموصى قال؛ لا يتبعها ولدها. ولو قال أوصيت لفلان بشاة من غنمي هذه فأعطوه شاة قد ولدت بعد موت الموصي ولداً قال يتبعها ولدها. ولو استهلك الوارث الولد قبل أن يعطي الشاة فلا ضمان عليه، وكذلك لو أوصى له بنخلة بأصلها ولم يقل من نخلي هذا فهي مثل الشاة التي أوصى بها ويعطونه أي نخلة شاؤوا دون ثمرتها التي أثمرتها في حياة الموصي أو بعد وفاته، وإن كانوا استهلكوا ذلك فلا ضمان عليهم
Book of Wills: For the testator, in our custom it is called a palm tree and it is standing, so its land is included. In Nawadir al-Mualla from Abu Yusuf: If a man bequeaths many palm trees or one palm tree, or gives as a gift, charity, or sale, he gets what is on the surface of the earth. And if he bequeaths a vineyard, garden, or cluster, he gets that with its root, and this palm tree is not like it. And al-Mualla mentioned from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths a palm tree to one person and its fruit to another, the bequest is valid, and the palm tree belongs to him with its root and land. And in Nawadir Ibn Samah from Muhammad: If he bequeaths a jar of oil, it is for the jar without the oil, and if he says 'jar of oil', it is for the jar alone. And if he bequeaths a ship of food, it is for the ship. Similarly, in these ways, in the narration of water and a basket of dates. And if he bequeaths to someone a scale, it includes the beam, two pans, and strings, but not the weights and cover. This is if it is unspecified; but if it is specific, it includes them. And Abu Yusuf said: If he bequeaths to a man the scale, he gets the two pans and beam, but not the weights. As for the steelyard, it includes its weight and pan. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad mentioned in Kitab al-Ikhtilaf from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths to a man a sword, he gets the blade without the sheath, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa. And from him that he gets the sword with its sheath, and the narration of Ibn Samah agrees with the original narration. And if he bequeaths a mushaf, and he has a cover when he bequeaths, he gets the mushaf without the cover according to Abu Hanifa. And in al-Biqali, if he bequeaths a Turkish tent, he gets it with its apparatus. So if he bequeaths a bridal canopy, he gets the covering without the sticks. And in it also from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths to a man a saddle, everything attached to it and contained in it is his, and nothing else. And al-Hasan mentioned in Kitab al-Ikhtilaf from Abu Yusuf concerning bequest of a saddle that he gets the two side-boards, stirrups, and the bridle, but not the servant's saddle-cloth nor the felt pad nor the girth. And Ibrahim mentioned from Muhammad concerning a man who died and freed his slave: He said, 'He gets his clothing and his belt.' And if he says 'his possessions', his sword and belt are included. Muhammad said: This is the will of Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak to his slave. And in Nawadir Bishr from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths to a man a sheep from his flock and does not say 'from this flock of mine', and the heirs give the legatee a sheep that gave birth after the testator's death, he said: Its offspring does not follow it. And if he said 'I bequeath to so-and-so a sheep from this flock of mine', and they give him a sheep that gave birth to an offspring after the testator's death, he said: Its offspring follows it. And if the heir consumes the offspring before giving the sheep, there is no liability. Similarly, if he bequeaths a palm tree with its root and does not say 'from this palm tree of mine', it is like the sheep bequeathed, and they give him any palm tree they wish without its fruit that it produced during the testator's life or after his death. And if they consumed that, there is no liability.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi rulings on what is included in a bequest of specific items. The author cites narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, often showing differences. The key principle is that the wording and context determine the scope. For a palm tree, the land is included if the tree is standing. Bequest of a vineyard or garden includes the root. For a jar of oil, the ruling depends on whether 'oil' is mentioned: if just 'jar of oil', only the jar is bequeathed; if 'jar of oil', it is clarified that only the jar is meant. Similarly for a ship of food, only the ship is given. For a scale, the beam, pans, and strings are included but not the weights and cover unless the scale is specifically identified. For a sword, Abu Hanifa holds that only the blade is bequeathed, while another narration includes the sheath. For a mushaf, the cover is excluded. For a saddle, items attached to it are included, but not items like the felt pad or girth. For a bequest of a sheep, if it is general ('from my flock'), the offspring born after death is not included; if specified ('from this flock'), the offspring follows. The same rule applies to a palm tree. If the heir consumes the offspring before delivery, there is no liability because the offspring was not part of the bequest.

Key Terms
نخلة (nakhla): A palm tree; when bequeathed and standing, its land is included.
كرم (karm): Vineyard; bequest includes the root (aṣl) but not the land.
بستان (bustān): Garden; same ruling as vineyard.
جمة (jumma): Cluster (of dates or grapes); includes the root.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does a bequest of a palm tree include if the tree is standing?
A) Only the tree itself.
B) The tree and its land.
C) The tree, its land, and all fruit.
D) Only the fruit.

Key Takeaway
A bequest of a standing palm tree includes the land; a vineyard bequest includes only the root.

Bequest of Containers and Scales: Wording Determines Scope
Rulings on bequests of containers and scales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that in bequests of containers and scales, the wording determines what is included, distinguishing between specified and unspecified items.

Core Idea
Bequest of a 'jar of oil' gives only the jar; bequest of a scale gives only the beam, pans, and strings unless specified.

When a testator bequeaths an item with a container or accessory, the exact wording matters. This lesson examines Hanafi rulings on bequests of jars, ships, scales, and steelyards, showing how the presence or absence of specification alters the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Classify the bequest by wording
Determine whether the bequest is for the container alone or the container plus its contents. For example, 'jar of oil' vs 'jar'.
The text shows that 'jar of oil' (zayt) means jar only.
2
Apply the container rule
For bequests like 'jar of oil' or 'ship of food', only the container (jar, ship) is given, not the contents.
The same applies to water and dates.
3
Analyze scale bequests
For a scale (mizān), if unspecified, the beam, pans, and strings are included but not weights or cover. If specified (bi-‘aynihi), all parts are included.
Abu Yusuf adds: for a steelyard (qabbān), it includes its weight and pan.
4
Note the difference between unspecified and specified
The ruling changes based on whether the item is identified specifically or generally.
Specification removes ambiguity and broadens inclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا للموصى عرفهم، وفي عرفنا تسمى نخلة وهي قائمة أيضاً فعليه تدخل أرضها. في نوادر المعلى عن أبي يوسف : أوصى لرجل نخل كثير أو نخلة واحدة أو وهب أو تصدق أو باع فله ما على ظهر الأرض، ولو أوصى له بكرم أو بستان أو جمة فله ذلك بأصله ولا يشبهه هذه النخلة، وذكر المعلى عن أبي يوسف : إذا أوصى بنخلة لإنسان ولآخر بثمرها فالوصية جائزة والنخل له بالنخل بأصله وأرضه وفي نوادر ابن سماعة عن محمد: إذا أوصى بزق زيت فهو على الزق دون الزيت ولو قال بزق الزيت فهو على الزق وحده، ولو بسفينة الطعام فهو على السفينة، وكذلك على هذه الوجوه في رواية الماء وقوصرة التمر. ولو أوصى لأحد بميزان فهو على العمود والكفتين والخيوط ولا يدخل فيه السنجات والغلاف، وهذا إذا كان بغير عينه، وأما إذا كان بعينه دخل فيه. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا أوصى لرجل بالميزان فله الكفتان والعمود ولا يمكن له السنجات، وأما القبان فهو له برمانته وكفته. وذكر الحسن بن زياد في كتاب الاختلاف عن أبي يوسف إذا أوصى لرجل بسيف فله النصل دون الجفن وهو قول أبي حنيفة. وعنه أن له السيف مع جفنه ورواية ابن سماعة موافقة لرواية الأصل. ولو أوصى بمصحف وله إذا أوصى غلاف فله المصحف دون الغلاف في قول أبي حنيفة . وفي البقالي له بقبة تركية فهو له بالآلة، فلو أوصى بحجلة فله الكسوة دون العيدان، وفيه أيضاً أبي يوسف : أوصى لرجل بسرج فكل شيء علق به وحرز فيه فهو له ولا يكون له غيره. وذكر الحسن في كتاب الاختلاف عن أبي يوسف في الوصية بالسرج أن له الدرفتين والركابين والمرة لا يكون للعبد والرفادة والصنقة. وذكر ابراهيم عن محمد في رجل مات فأعتق عبده قال : له كسوته ومنطقته . وإن قال متاعه يدخل فيه سيفه ومنطقته قال محمد هي وصية عبد الله بن المبارك لغلامه وفي نوارد بشر عن أبي يوسف أوصى لرجل بشاة من غنمه ولم يقل من غنمي هذه فأعطى الورثة الموصى له شاة قد ولدت بعد موت الموصى قال؛ لا يتبعها ولدها. ولو قال أوصيت لفلان بشاة من غنمي هذه فأعطوه شاة قد ولدت بعد موت الموصي ولداً قال يتبعها ولدها. ولو استهلك الوارث الولد قبل أن يعطي الشاة فلا ضمان عليه، وكذلك لو أوصى له بنخلة بأصلها ولم يقل من نخلي هذا فهي مثل الشاة التي أوصى بها ويعطونه أي نخلة شاؤوا دون ثمرتها التي أثمرتها في حياة الموصي أو بعد وفاته، وإن كانوا استهلكوا ذلك فلا ضمان عليهم
Book of Wills: For the testator, in our custom it is called a palm tree and it is standing, so its land is included. In Nawadir al-Mualla from Abu Yusuf: If a man bequeaths many palm trees or one palm tree, or gives as a gift, charity, or sale, he gets what is on the surface of the earth. And if he bequeaths a vineyard, garden, or cluster, he gets that with its root, and this palm tree is not like it. And al-Mualla mentioned from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths a palm tree to one person and its fruit to another, the bequest is valid, and the palm tree belongs to him with its root and land. And in Nawadir Ibn Samah from Muhammad: If he bequeaths a jar of oil, it is for the jar without the oil, and if he says 'jar of oil', it is for the jar alone. And if he bequeaths a ship of food, it is for the ship. Similarly, in these ways, in the narration of water and a basket of dates. And if he bequeaths to someone a scale, it includes the beam, two pans, and strings, but not the weights and cover. This is if it is unspecified; but if it is specific, it includes them. And Abu Yusuf said: If he bequeaths to a man the scale, he gets the two pans and beam, but not the weights. As for the steelyard, it includes its weight and pan. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad mentioned in Kitab al-Ikhtilaf from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths to a man a sword, he gets the blade without the sheath, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa. And from him that he gets the sword with its sheath, and the narration of Ibn Samah agrees with the original narration. And in al-Biqali, if he bequeaths a Turkish tent, he gets it with its apparatus. So if he bequeaths a bridal canopy, he gets the covering without the sticks. And if he said 'I bequeath to so-and-so a sheep from this flock of mine', and they give him a sheep that gave birth to an offspring after the testator's death, he said: Its offspring follows it. And if the heir consumes the offspring before giving the sheep, there is no liability. Similarly, if he bequeaths a palm tree with its root and does not say 'from this palm tree of mine', it is like the sheep bequeathed, and they give him any palm tree they wish without its fruit that it produced during the testator's life or after his death. And if they consumed that, there is no liability.

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi rulings on what is included in a bequest of specific items. The author cites narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, often showing differences. The key principle is that the wording and context determine the scope. For a palm tree, the land is included if the tree is standing. Bequest of a vineyard or garden includes the root. For a jar of oil, the ruling depends on whether 'oil' is mentioned: if just 'jar of oil', only the jar is bequeathed; if 'jar of oil', it is clarified that only the jar is meant. Similarly for a ship of food, only the ship is given. For a scale, the beam, pans, and strings are included but not the weights and cover unless the scale is specifically identified. For a sword, Abu Hanifa holds that only the blade is bequeathed, while another narration includes the sheath. For a mushaf, the cover is excluded. For a saddle, items attached to it are included, but not items like the felt pad or girth. For a bequest of a sheep, if it is general ('from my flock'), the offspring born after death is not included; if specified ('from this flock'), the offspring follows. The same rule applies to a palm tree. If the heir consumes the offspring before delivery, there is no liability because the offspring was not part of the bequest.

Key Terms
زق زيت (ziqq zayt): A jar of oil; in a bequest, only the jar is given.
ميزان (mizān): A scale; if unspecified only beam, pans, strings included.
قبان (qabbān): A steelyard; includes its weight and pan.
سفينة الطعام (safīnat al-ṭa‘ām): A ship of food; only the ship is bequeathed.

Checkpoint
What does a bequest of a scale (ميزان) include if the scale is unspecified?
A) Beam, pans, strings.
B) Beam, pans, strings, weights, and cover.
C) Beam only.
D) Pans and strings only.

Key Takeaway
In bequests of containers and scales, the wording and specification decide what is included: default is minimal, specification broadens.

Bequest of Swords, Mushafs, and Saddles: Accessories Included or Not
Rulings on bequests of swords, mushafs, tents, and saddles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on whether accessories like sheaths, covers, and saddle fittings are included in bequests of swords, mushafs, and saddles.

Core Idea
A bequeathed sword includes only the blade; a mushaf excludes its cover; a saddle includes attached items but not separate cloths.

Bequests of items with detachable parts require careful analysis. This lesson covers Hanafi rulings on swords (sheath), mushafs (cover), Turkish tents and canopies (apparatus), and saddles (attached vs separate items), showing where the boundaries lie.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item and its parts
Determine the primary object (sword, mushaf, saddle) and what accessories are typically attached or separate.
For a sword, the blade is primary; the sheath is an accessory.
2
Apply the default rule for each
Abu Hanifa: sword bequest includes only the blade (nassl), not the sheath (jafn). For mushaf, the cover (ghilāf) is excluded. For a saddle, everything attached and contained (e.g., stirrups) is included, but separate items like the felt pad (rifāda) are not.
There is a difference of narration for the sword; one version includes the sheath.
3
Check for ikhtilaf
Note that for the sword, there is an alternative narration from Abu Yusuf that includes the sheath. The original narration (also from Ibn Samah) agrees with Abu Hanifa.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one excluding the sheath.
4
Apply the tent and canopy rulings
A Turkish tent (qubba turkiyya) includes its apparatus (āla); a bridal canopy (hajla) includes only the covering (kiswa), not the sticks.
These rulings show a pattern: what is essential for the item's function is included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا للموصى عرفهم، وفي عرفنا تسمى نخلة وهي قائمة أيضاً فعليه تدخل أرضها. في نوادر المعلى عن أبي يوسف : أوصى لرجل نخل كثير أو نخلة واحدة أو وهب أو تصدق أو باع فله ما على ظهر الأرض، ولو أوصى له بكرم أو بستان أو جمة فله ذلك بأصله ولا يشبهه هذه النخلة، وذكر المعلى عن أبي يوسف : إذا أوصى بنخلة لإنسان ولآخر بثمرها فالوصية جائزة والنخل له بالنخل بأصله وأرضه وفي نوادر ابن سماعة عن محمد: إذا أوصى بزق زيت فهو على الزق دون الزيت ولو قال بزق الزيت فهو على الزق وحده، ولو بسفينة الطعام فهو على السفينة، وكذلك على هذه الوجوه في رواية الماء وقوصرة التمر. ولو أوصى لأحد بميزان فهو على العمود والكفتين والخيوط ولا يدخل فيه السنجات والغلاف، وهذا إذا كان بغير عينه، وأما إذا كان بعينه دخل فيه. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا أوصى لرجل بالميزان فله الكفتان والعمود ولا يمكن له السنجات، وأما القبان فهو له برمانته وكفته. وذكر الحسن بن زياد في كتاب الاختلاف عن أبي يوسف إذا أوصى لرجل بسيف فله النصل دون الجفن وهو قول أبي حنيفة. وعنه أن له السيف مع جفنه ورواية ابن سماعة موافقة لرواية الأصل. ولو أوصى بمصحف وله إذا أوصى غلاف فله المصحف دون الغلاف في قول أبي حنيفة . وفي البقالي له بقبة تركية فهو له بالآلة، فلو أوصى بحجلة فله الكسوة دون العيدان، وفيه أيضاً أبي يوسف : أوصى لرجل بسرج فكل شيء علق به وحرز فيه فهو له ولا يكون له غيره. وذكر الحسن في كتاب الاختلاف عن أبي يوسف في الوصية بالسرج أن له الدرفتين والركابين والمرة لا يكون للعبد والرفادة والصنقة. وذكر ابراهيم عن محمد في رجل مات فأعتق عبده قال : له كسوته ومنطقته . وإن قال متاعه يدخل فيه سيفه ومنطقته قال محمد هي وصية عبد الله بن المبارك لغلامه وفي نوارد بشر عن أبي يوسف أوصى لرجل بشاة من غنمه ولم يقل من غنمي هذه فأعطى الورثة الموصى له شاة قد ولدت بعد موت الموصى قال؛ لا يتبعها ولدها. ولو قال أوصيت لفلان بشاة من غنمي هذه فأعطوه شاة قد ولدت بعد موت الموصي ولداً قال يتبعها ولدها. ولو استهلك الوارث الولد قبل أن يعطي الشاة فلا ضمان عليه، وكذلك لو أوصى له بنخلة بأصلها ولم يقل من نخلي هذا فهي مثل الشاة التي أوصى بها ويعطونه أي نخلة شاؤوا دون ثمرتها التي أثمرتها في حياة الموصي أو بعد وفاته، وإن كانوا استهلكوا ذلك فلا ضمان عليهم
Book of Wills: For the testator, in our custom it is called a palm tree and it is standing, so its land is included. In Nawadir al-Mualla from Abu Yusuf: If a man bequeaths many palm trees or one palm tree, or gives as a gift, charity, or sale, he gets what is on the surface of the earth. And if he bequeaths a vineyard, garden, or cluster, he gets that with its root, and this palm tree is not like it. And al-Mualla mentioned from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths a palm tree to one person and its fruit to another, the bequest is valid, and the palm tree belongs to him with its root and land. And in Nawadir Ibn Samah from Muhammad: If he bequeaths a jar of oil, it is for the jar without the oil, and if he says 'jar of oil', it is for the jar alone. And if he bequeaths a ship of food, it is for the ship. Similarly, in these ways, in the narration of water and a basket of dates. And if he bequeaths to someone a scale, it includes the beam, two pans, and strings, but not the weights and cover. This is if it is unspecified; but if it is specific, it includes them. And Abu Yusuf said: If he bequeaths to a man the scale, he gets the two pans and beam, but not the weights. As for the steelyard, it includes its weight and pan. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad mentioned in Kitab al-Ikhtilaf from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths to a man a sword, he gets the blade without the sheath, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa. And from him that he gets the sword with its sheath, and the narration of Ibn Samah agrees with the original narration. And if he bequeaths a mushaf, and he has a cover when he bequeaths, he gets the mushaf without the cover according to Abu Hanifa. And in al-Biqali, if he bequeaths a Turkish tent, he gets it with its apparatus. So if he bequeaths a bridal canopy, he gets the covering without the sticks. And in it also from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths to a man a saddle, everything attached to it and contained in it is his, and nothing else. And al-Hasan mentioned in Kitab al-Ikhtilaf from Abu Yusuf concerning bequest of a saddle that he gets the two side-boards, stirrups, and the bridle, but not the servant's saddle-cloth nor the felt pad nor the girth. And Ibrahim mentioned from Muhammad concerning a man who died and freed his slave: He said, 'He gets his clothing and his belt.' And if he says 'his possessions', his sword and belt are included. Muhammad said: This is the will of Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak to his slave. And in Nawadir Bishr from Abu Yusuf: If he bequeaths to a man a sheep from his flock and does not say 'from this flock of mine', and the heirs give the legatee a sheep that gave birth after the testator's death, he said: Its offspring does not follow it. And if he said 'I bequeath to so-and-so a sheep from this flock of mine', and they give him a sheep that gave birth to an offspring after the testator's death, he said: Its offspring follows it. And if the heir consumes the offspring before giving the sheep, there is no liability. Similarly, if he bequeaths a palm tree with its root and does not say 'from this palm tree of mine', it is like the sheep bequeathed, and they give him any palm tree they wish without its fruit that it produced during the testator's life or after his death. And if they consumed that, there is no liability.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi rulings on what is included in a bequest of specific items. The author cites narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, often showing differences. The key principle is that the wording and context determine the scope. For a palm tree, the land is included if the tree is standing. Bequest of a vineyard or garden includes the root. For a jar of oil, the ruling depends on whether 'oil' is mentioned: if just 'jar of oil', only the jar is bequeathed; if 'jar of oil', it is clarified that only the jar is meant. Similarly for a ship of food, only the ship is given. For a scale, the beam, pans, and strings are included but not the weights and cover unless the scale is specifically identified. For a sword, Abu Hanifa holds that only the blade is bequeathed, while another narration includes the sheath. For a mushaf, the cover is excluded. For a saddle, items attached to it are included, but not items like the felt pad or girth. For a bequest of a sheep, if it is general ('from my flock'), the offspring born after death is not included; if specified ('from this flock'), the offspring follows. The same rule applies to a palm tree. If the heir consumes the offspring before delivery, there is no liability because the offspring was not part of the bequest.

Key Terms
نصل (nassl): Blade of a sword; included in bequest.
جفن (jafn): Sheath of a sword; excluded from bequest.
غلاف (ghilāf): Cover of a mushaf; excluded.
سرج (sarij): Saddle; attached items included, separate items excluded.
رفادة (rifāda): Felt pad under saddle; excluded.
صنقة (ṣanqa): Girth; excluded from saddle bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what does a bequest of a mushaf (copy of the Quran) include if the testator had a cover?
A) The mushaf with its cover.
B) Only the mushaf, not the cover.
C) Only the cover.
D) Neither the mushaf nor the cover.

Key Takeaway
For items with accessories, the Hanafi school generally excludes separate coverings and includes only essential attached parts.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Bequest of Sheep and Palm Trees: General vs Specific Wording
Ruling on bequest of sheep and palm trees with general vs specific wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a bequest is general (e.g., 'a sheep from my flock'), the legatee does not receive offspring born after death; if specific ('from this flock'), the offspring follows.

Core Idea
General bequest gives only the mother; specific bequest includes offspring born after death.

The final section of this passage deals with bequests of sheep and palm trees when the testator uses general or specific language. The ruling turns on whether the testator says 'from my flock' (general) or 'from this flock of mine' (specific). This lesson explains the difference and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Classify the wording as general or specific
Check if the testator says 'a sheep from my flock' (min ghanamī) vs 'a sheep from this flock of mine' (min ghanamī hādhihī). The latter is specific.
The same distinction applies to palm trees with root.
2
Apply the rule for offspring
If general, offspring born after death does not follow the mother. If specific, it does follow.
The offspring is considered separate property unless specified.
3
Apply liability rule
If the heir consumes the offspring before giving the mother, there is no liability on the heir.
Because the offspring was not part of the bequest.
4
Analogous rule for palm trees
If a palm tree is bequeathed with its root (bi-aṣlihā) but not specified ('from this palm tree'), the heir can give any palm tree, and its fruit (produced before or after death) is not included.
If the heir consumed the fruit, no liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا للموصى عرفهم، وفي عرفنا تسمى نخلة وهي قائمة أيضاً فعليه تدخل أرضها. في نوادر المعلى عن أبي يوسف : أوصى لرجل نخل كثير أو نخلة واحدة أو وهب أو تصدق أو باع فله ما على ظهر الأرض، ولو أوصى له بكرم أو بستان أو جمة فله ذلك بأصله ولا يشبهه هذه النخلة، وذكر المعلى عن أبي يوسف : إذا أوصى بنخلة لإنسان ولآخر بثمرها فالوصية جائزة والنخل له بالنخل بأصله وأرضه وفي نوادر ابن سماعة عن محمد: إذا أوصى بزق زيت فهو على الزق دون الزيت ولو قال بزق الزيت فهو على الزق وحده، ولو بسفينة الطعام فهو على السفينة، وكذلك على هذه الوجوه في رواية الماء وقوصرة التمر. ولو أوصى لأحد بميزان فهو على العمود والكفتين والخيوط ولا يدخل فيه السنجات والغلاف، وهذا إذا كان بغير عينه، وأما إذا كان بعينه دخل فيه. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا أوصى لرجل بالميزان فله الكفتان والعمود ولا يمكن له السنجات، وأما القبان فهو له برمانته وكفته. وذكر الحسن بن زياد في كتاب الاختلاف عن أبي يوسف إذا أوصى لرجل بسيف فله النصل دون الجفن وهو قول أبي حنيفة. وعنه أن له السيف مع جفنه ورواية ابن سماعة موافقة لرواية الأصل. ولو أوصى بمصحف وله إذا أوصى غلاف فله المصحف دون الغلاف في قول أبي حنيفة . وفي البقالي له بقبة تركية فهو له بالآلة، فلو أوصى بحجلة فله الكسوة دون العيدان، وفيه أيضاً أبي يوسف : أوصى لرجل بسرج فكل شيء علق به وحرز فيه فهو له ولا يكون له غيره. وذكر الحسن في كتاب الاختلاف عن أبي يوسف في الوصية بالسرج أن له الدرفتين والركابين والمرة لا يكون للعبد والرفادة والصنقة. وذكر ابراهيم عن محمد في رجل مات فأعتق عبده قال : له كسوته ومنطقته . وإن قال متاعه يدخل فيه سيفه ومنطقته قال محمد هي وصية عبد الله بن المبارك لغلامه وفي نوارد بشر عن أبي يوسف أوصى لرجل بشاة من غنمه ولم يقل من غنمي هذه فأعطى الورثة الموصى له شاة قد ولدت بعد موت الموصى قال؛ لا يتبعها ولدها. ولو قال أوصيت لفلان بشاة من غنمي هذه فأعطوه شاة قد ولدت بعد موت الموصي ولداً قال يتبعها ولدها. ولو استهلك الوارث الولد قبل أن يعطي الشاة فلا ضمان عليه، وكذلك لو أوصى له بنخلة بأصلها ولم يقل من نخلي هذا فهي مثل الشاة التي أوصى بها ويعطونه أي نخلة شاؤوا دون ثمرتها التي أثمرتها في حياة الموصي أو بعد وفاته، وإن كانوا استهلكوا ذلك فلا ضمان عليهم

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi rulings on what is included in a bequest of specific items. The author cites narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, often showing differences. The key principle is that the wording and context determine the scope. For a palm tree, the land is included if the tree is standing. Bequest of a vineyard or garden includes the root. For a jar of oil, the ruling depends on whether 'oil' is mentioned: if just 'jar of oil', only the jar is bequeathed; if 'jar of oil', it is clarified that only the jar is meant. Similarly for a ship of food, only the ship is given. For a scale, the beam, pans, and strings are included but not the weights and cover unless the scale is specifically identified. For a sword, Abu Hanifa holds that only the blade is bequeathed, while another narration includes the sheath. For a mushaf, the cover is excluded. For a saddle, items attached to it are included, but not items like the felt pad or girth. The same rule applies to a palm tree. If the heir consumes the offspring before delivery, there is no liability because the offspring was not part of the bequest.

Key Terms
شاة (shāh): Sheep; bequest rules depend on wording.
غنم (ghanam): Flock of sheep; general vs specific matters.
ولد (walad): Offspring of a sheep; included only if specific.
ثمرة (thamara): Fruit of a palm tree; not included in general bequest.

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths 'a sheep from this flock of mine' (specific). After death, the sheep gives birth. What does the legatee receive?
A) Only the sheep.

D) Nothing, because the bequest is void.

Key Takeaway

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Bequest of a Slave Girl: Effect of Posthumous Birth
Rulings on bequest of a slave girl when she gives birth after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether offspring born after the testator's death are included in a bequest of a slave girl, and distinguish between bequests of freedom versus transfer of ownership.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a slave girl’s post-death offspring follow the bequest only in transfers of ownership, not in personal emancipation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rules on bequests of a slave girl when she gives birth after the testator's death. The key distinction hinges on whether the bequest involves freeing the slave (itq or kitaba) or transferring ownership (sale, charity, gift). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly executing bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of bequest
Determine whether the testator bequeathed freedom (itq), a contract of kitaba, sale to a specific person, charity, or gift. Each type yields a different ruling on the offspring.
Focus on the testator's wording: 'free' vs 'sell' vs 'give in charity'.
2
Note the timing of the birth
Confirm that the child was born after the testator's death but before the bequest was executed. This timing triggers the rule.
If the child was born before death, it would be part of the estate and included in the bequest if the slave girl is bequeathed.
3
Apply the rule for freedom or kitaba
If the bequest is for itq or kitaba, the mother is freed (or becomes mukataba) but the child is not included. The child remains a slave of the heirs.
The text states: 'عتقت الجارية ولم يعتق الولد'.
4
Apply the rule for transfer of ownership
If the bequest is for charity, gift, or sale for charity, the child is included and follows the mother. But if the bequest is a sale to a specific person for a price, the child is not included.
Charity/gift: child included; sale to named buyer: child not included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يتصل بهذا الفصل ما إذا أوصى أن تعتق جاريته هذه بعد موته ومات فقبل أن تعتق ولدت ولداً فهي مع ولدها يخرجان من عتقت الجارية ولم يعتق الولد وكذا لو أوصى بأن يكاتب هذه الجارية بعد موته أو أوصى أن تباع هي من نفسها أو تعتق على مال فولدت ولداً بعد موت الموصى لا تنفذ الوصية في الولد. ولو أوصى أن يتصدق بجاريته هذه على المساكين أو على فلان أو توهب من فلان فولدت ولداً بعد موته فتنفذ الوصية في الولد كما تنفذ في الجارية، ولو أوصى بأن تباع جاريته هذه فلان بألف من درهم فولدت ولداً بعد موت الموصي بيعت هي ولا يباع ولدها. ولو أوصى بأن تباع جاريته هذه ويتصدق بثمنها على المساكين أو على فلان فولدت الجارية بعد موته ولداً فإنه تنفذ الوصية في الولد ولو أوصى بأن تباع جاريته هذه من فلان بألف درهم فجاء عبد وقتلها فدفع بها أو قطع يدها فدفع بيدها أو وطئها وطأ بشبهة حتى غرم العقر فإنه لا يباع العبد المدفوع ولا الأرش ولا العقر فبعد ذلك ينظر؛ إن كانت قد قتلت بطلت الوصية لفقدان محلها، وإن كانت قد قطعت يدها بيعت من الموصي له بنصف الثمن إن شاء، ولو وطئت وهي ثيب لم ينقصها الوطء لا يحط شيء من الثمن، وكذلك إذا تلفت عينها أو يدها بآفة سماوية بيعت بجميع الثمن المشتري إلا إذا صارت إليه أصلاً فصار له حصته من الثمن، ولو أوصى بأن تباع جاريته هذه من فلان بألف درهم ويتصدق بثمنها على المساكين فأبى فلان البيع بطلت الوصيتان جميعاً، وكذلك لو قتلت الجارية بعد موت الموصي وغرم القاتل قيمتها بطلت الوصيتان، وكذلك لو أوصى أن تكاتب جاريته ويتصدق ببدل الكتابة أو تباع من نفسها ويتصدق بثمنها على المساكين فولدت بعد موته ولداً بيعت هي وحدها ولم يبع معها ولدها
And what is connected to this section: when he bequeaths that this slave girl of his be freed after his death, and he dies, and before she is freed she gives birth to a child, then she and her child come out (of the estate), the slave girl is freed but the child is not freed. Similarly, if he bequeaths that she be made a mukataba after his death, or bequeaths that she be sold to herself or be freed for a price, and she gives birth after the testator's death, the bequest does not apply to the child. And if he bequeaths that his slave girl be given in charity to the poor or to so-and-so, or be given as a gift to so-and-so, and she gives birth after his death, then the bequest applies to the child as it applies to the slave girl. And if he bequeaths that this slave girl of his be sold to so-and-so for a thousand dirhams, and she gives birth after the testator's death, she is sold and her child is not sold. And if he bequeaths that his slave girl be sold and its price be given in charity to the poor or to so-and-so, and the slave girl gives birth after his death, then the bequest applies to the child. And if he bequeaths that his slave girl be sold to so-and-so for a thousand dirhams, and a slave comes and kills her, so he pays compensation for her, or cuts off her hand, so he pays compensation for her hand, or has intercourse with her with a doubtful act so that he pays the dower, then the slave who is paid in compensation, nor the blood money, nor the dower is sold. After that, it is considered: if she was killed, the bequest is void due to the loss of its subject. And if her hand was cut off, she is sold to the legatee for half the price if he wishes. And if she was cohabited with while she was a virgin, it does not decrease her value; nothing is deducted from the price. Similarly, if her eye or hand is lost due to a heavenly affliction, she is sold for the entire price; but if the thing became his property initially, then he gets his share of the price. And if he bequeaths that his slave girl be sold to so-and-so for a thousand dirhams and the price be given in charity to the poor, and so-and-so refuses to buy, both bequests are void. Similarly, if the slave girl is killed after the testator's death and the killer pays her value, both bequests are void. Similarly, if he bequeaths that she be made a mukataba and the value of the kitaba be given in charity, or be sold to herself and its price be given in charity to the poor, and she gives birth after his death, she alone is sold and her child is not sold with her.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage presents a series of detailed Hanafi rulings on bequests involving a slave girl (jariya) when events occur between the testator's death and the execution of the bequest. The key distinction is based on the nature of the bequest. If the bequest is for freeing (itq) or making a contract of kitaba (mukataba), the offspring born after death does not share in the freedom or kitaba; the mother is freed but the child remains a slave. However, if the bequest is for charity (sadaqa) or gift (hiba), the offspring is included and follows the mother. When the bequest is to sell the slave girl to a specific person for a price, and she gives birth, only she is sold and not the child. But if the sale is for charity, the child is included in the charity. When the slave girl is killed or injured by a third party after the testator's death, the compensation is not part of the bequest; the bequest is void if she is killed, or she is sold at a reduced price if injured. If the intended buyer refuses, both bequests become void. The rulings are based on the principle that the offspring follows the mother only in certain types of bequests, particularly those that involve transfer of ownership rather than personal emancipation.

Key Terms
جارية (jāriya): A female slave; the subject of various bequests and rulings on offspring.
عتق (itq): Emancipation or freeing of a slave; a bequest of itq applies only to the mother, not to offspring born after death.
مكاتبة (mukātaba): A contract of kitaba (manumission by payment); similar to itq in that offspring are not included.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man bequeaths that his slave girl be freed after his death, and she gives birth after his death but before being freed, what is the ruling?
A) Both mother and child are freed.
B) The mother is freed, and the child also becomes free if the heirs consent.
C) The mother is freed, and the child is not freed.
D) The child is freed instead of the mother.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest of emancipation (itq or kitaba) applies only to the slave girl herself, not to children born after the testator's death, while bequests of charity or gift include the offspring.

Distinguishing Between a Will and an Acknowledgment in Wording
Explaining how different phrasings determine whether a statement is a will or an acknowledgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a will (wasaya) and an acknowledgment (iqrar) based on the wording used, and apply the Hanafi ruling that certain phrasings are considered wills by istihsan.

Core Idea
The phrasing of the statement determines whether it is a will or an acknowledgment; the word 'an' after 'awsaytu' changes the ruling.

In Hanafi law, the validity and effect of a disposition of property after death depends on the exact words used. A statement may be a will, an acknowledgment, or even a gift. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqaiq, explains the critical distinction between a will and an acknowledgment based on the phrasing, especially the use of the subordinating 'an'. Understanding this distinction is essential for drafting valid wills and avoiding disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrasings and their rulings
Focus on the pair: 'Ashhadu anni awsaytu li-fulan bi-alf dirham' (I bequeathed to so-and-so) vs 'Awsaytu anna li-fulan fi mali alf dirham' (I bequeath that so-and-so has a thousand in my wealth). According to Imam Muhammad, the first is a will, the second is an acknowledgment.
The difference hinges on the presence of 'an' after 'awsaytu'.
2
Understand the linguistic basis
When 'awsaytu' enters upon the subordinating 'an', it changes meaning to 'I mentioned' (dhakartu). Therefore, the second statement is merely an acknowledgment, not a will.
This is a key principle in Hanafi linguistics for interpreting legal statements.
3
Apply to other examples from the text
Consider variations: 'sudd dari li-fulan' (a sixth of my house to so-and-so) in a will is a will; but 'li-fulan sudd fi dari' (to so-and-so a sixth in my house) is an acknowledgment. Note the change in wording order and preposition.
The location of 'fi' (in) changes the meaning.
4
Recognize the role of istihsan over qiyas
Certain phrasings, like 'li-fulan dirhamun min mali' (to so-and-so a dirham from my wealth), are considered wills by istihsan even though qiyas might suggest otherwise. Istihsan favors the intention of the testator when the context indicates a will.
Istihsan is a distinctive Hanafi tool that overrides strict analogy.
5
Determine when possession is required
If a statement lacks explicit will wording (e.g., 'this slave of mine is for so-and-so') and is not in a will context, it is a gift (hiba) requiring possession during life. If mentioned in a will context or with 'after my death', it is a will and possession is not required before death.
Possession (qabd) is a key differentiator between gifts and wills.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان الألفاظ التي تكون وصية والتي لا تكون وصية روى ابن سماعة في نوادره عن محمد: إذا قال الرجل أشهدوا أني أوصيت لفلان بألف درهم وأوصيت بأن لفلان في مالي ألف درهم فالألف الأولى وصية والأخرى إقرار والفرق أن أوصيت لما دخلت على «أن» المصدرية تستعمل بمعنى ذكرت ولهذا كان إقراراً بخلاف الأولى فإنها على بابها . وفي الأصل : إذا قال في وصيته سدس داري لفلان وأني أجيز ذلك يكون وصية، ولو قال سدس في داري لفلان وإني أجيز ذلك يكون وصية، ولو قال لفلان سدس في داري فإنه يكون إقراراً، وعلى هذا إذا قال الرجل لفلان درهم من مالي يكون وصية استحساناً، وإن كان في ذكر وصيته إذا قال في مالي كان إقراراً، وإذا قال عبدي هذا لفلان وذاري هذه لفلان ولم يقل وصية ولا كان في ذكر وصيه ولا بعد موتي كانت هبة قياساً واستحساناً، وإن قبضها في حال حياته صح، وإن لم يقبضها حتى مات فهو باطل، وإن ذكرها في خلال الوصية ذكر الشيخ الإمام الزاهد أحمد الطواويسي في شرح وصايا الأصل القياس أن يكون هذا وصية، وفي الاستحسان لا يكون وصية. وإذا قال أوصيت أن يوهب لفلان سدس داري بعد موتي كان ذلك وصية عملاً بقوله بعد موتي فالهبة بعد الموت هي الوصية فتصح مع الشيوع ولا يشترط قبضه في حيات الموصي . ولو قال ثلثي مالي لفلان أو قال سدس مالي لفلان ثم مات قبل أن يقبض فالقياس أن يكون هذا باطلاً، وفي الاستحسان يكون وصية جائزة وتأويله إذا قال ذلك في خلال الوصايا يكون وصية ظاهرة فصار كأنه قال ثلث مالي وصية لفلان ولو قال هكذا فإنه جائز، وإن كان قبل القبض، وكذلك إذا قال بعد موتي لأنه لما قال بعد موتي فإنه نص على الوصية بخلاف ما إذا قال في صحته ثلث مالي لفلان لأنه
And as for the explanation of the expressions that constitute a will and those that do not: Ibn Samah narrated in his Nawadir from Muhammad: If a man says 'Bear witness that I have bequeathed to so-and-so a thousand dirhams' and 'I have bequeathed that so-and-so has a thousand dirhams in my wealth', the first thousand is a will and the other is an acknowledgment. The difference is that 'I have bequeathed' when it enters upon the subordinating 'an' is used in the sense of 'I have mentioned', and therefore it is an acknowledgment, unlike the first which is used in its proper sense. And in al-Asl: If he says in his will 'a sixth of my house to so-and-so and I authorize that', it is a will. And if he says 'a sixth in my house to so-and-so and I authorize that', it is a will. And if he says 'to so-and-so a sixth in my house', it is an acknowledgment. And on this basis, if a man says 'to so-and-so a dirham from my wealth', it is a will by istihsan, even though when he says 'in my wealth' in the context of his will, it is an acknowledgment. And if he says 'this slave of mine is for so-and-so' and 'these offspring of mine are for so-and-so', and he does not say 'will' nor was it in the context of his will nor 'after my death', it is a gift by qiyas and istihsan. If he takes possession during his life, it is valid; if he does not take possession until he dies, it is void. And if he mentions it in the midst of a will, Shaykh Imam al-Zahid Ahmad al-Tawawisi mentioned in his commentary on Wsaya al-Asl that by qiyas this would be a will, and by istihsan it is not a will. And if he says 'I bequeath that a sixth of my house be given to so-and-so after my death', that is a will, acting on his statement 'after my death', for a gift after death is a will. It is valid even with common ownership, and possession during the testator's life is not a condition. And if he says 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so' or 'one-sixth of my wealth to so-and-so', then dies before possession, by qiyas this is void, but by istihsan it is a valid will. Its interpretation is that if he says it in the context of wills, it is an apparent will, so it is as if he said 'one-third of my wealth is a will for so-and-so'. If he says such, it is valid even before possession. Similarly, if he says 'after my death', because when he says 'after my death', he explicitly states a will, unlike if he says in his health 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so' because...
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the crucial distinction between a will (wasaya) and an acknowledgment (iqrar) based on the wording used. The central ruling is from Imam Muhammad: saying 'Ashhadu anni awsaytu li-fulan bi-alf dirham' (I bequeathed) is a will, while 'Awsaytu anna li-fulan fi mali alf dirham' (I bequeath that so-and-so has a thousand in my wealth) is an acknowledgment. The difference is that when 'awsaytu' enters upon the subordinating 'an', it means 'I mentioned' (dhakartu), making it an acknowledgment. The passage also gives examples from the original text (al-Asl): saying 'sudd dari li-fulan' (a sixth of my house to so-and-so) in a will is a will, but 'li-fulan sudd fi dari' (to so-and-so a sixth in my house) is an acknowledgment. Several rulings are based on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas. For instance, saying 'li-fulan dirhamun min mali' (to so-and-so a dirham from my wealth) is considered a will by istihsan, though qiyas might suggest otherwise. The passage also discusses gifts (hiba) and the condition of possession. If someone says 'abdi hadha li-fulan' (this slave of mine is for so-and-so) without mentioning will or death, it is a gift and requires possession during life. If mentioned in a will context, it is treated differently. The key principle is that explicit words like 'after my death' (ba'd mauti) make it clearly a will. If a person says 'thuluth mali li-fulan' (one-third of my wealth to so-and-so) in his health, by qiyas it is void because it is a gift before death without possession, but by istihsan it is a valid will because the context of wills makes it a bequest.

Key Terms
وصية (wasīya): A will or bequest; a disposition of property that takes effect after death.
إقرار (iqrār): An acknowledgment of a debt or right; it binds the estate as a debt, not as a bequest.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of legal reasoning that departs from strict analogy for a more equitable result.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both are valid wills.
B) The first is a will, the second is an acknowledgment.
C) The first is an acknowledgment, the second is a will.
D) Both are invalid.

Key Takeaway
The phrasing of a bequest determines whether it is a will (wasaya) or an acknowledgment (iqrar); the word 'an' after 'awsaytu' changes the ruling.

Distinguishing Wasiyya from Hibah through Explicit Linkage to Death
Defining when a statement becomes a will versus a gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make a statement a will (wasiyya) versus a gift (hibah), and identify invalid formulations according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A statement is a will only if it explicitly mentions death, is placed in the context of wills, or links the transfer to after death.

When a person during their lifetime makes a statement that could be interpreted as either a gift or a will, the Hanafi school provides clear criteria to determine its nature. The key is whether the statement is explicitly tied to death, either by direct mention, context, or linkage to the afterlife. This lesson unpacks these criteria and illustrates them with practical examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Read the first part of the passage: if the person did not explicitly state a will, mention it in the course of wills, or link it to after death, the statement is considered a gift (hibah).
The default is hibah unless death is referenced.
2
Recognize the exceptions
If the statement mentions 'if an event happens to me' (implying death) or 'from my third' (thuluthi), it is a will even without explicit death mention. Note that 'from my third' refers to the one-third of the estate reserved for bequests.
'From my third' is specific, while 'from a third of my wealth' is indefinite.
3
Distinguish valid and invalid formulations
The passage states that saying 'from a third of my wealth', 'from half', or 'from a quarter' is invalid (batil) because the fraction is not attached to the estate in a way that clearly reserves it for a bequest. 'From my third' is valid because it refers to the known one-third portion.
The key is specificity: 'thuluthi' (my third) vs 'thuluth mal' (a third of wealth).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يصرح بالوصية ولا ذكرها في خلال الوصايا ولا إضافة إلى ما بعد الموت فلا يجعل وصية بل يجعل هبة لو ذكرها في خلال الوصايا أو إضافة إلى ما بعد الموت وكان ذلك في حال الصحة يكون وصية والحاصل لا فرق بين حالة الصحة وحالة المرض، وروى محمد عن أبي يوسف وعن أبي حنيفة في رجل قال في مرضه أو في صحته إن حدث لي حادث فلفلان كذا هذا وصية، وكذلك لو قال لفلان ألف درهم من ثلثي فهذا وصية وإن لم يذكر فيها الموت، ولو قال لفلان ألف درهم من ثلث مالي أو قال من نصف مالي أو قال من ربع مالي فهو باطل
He did not explicitly state a will, nor mention it in the course of wills, nor link it to after death; so it is not made a will but is made a gift. If he mentioned it in the course of wills or linked it to after death, and that was in a state of health, it becomes a will. The conclusion is that there is no difference between the state of health and the state of illness. Muhammad narrated from Abu Yusuf and from Abu Hanifa regarding a man who said in his illness or in his health: 'If an event happens to me, then so-and-so gets such-and-such' — this is a will. Similarly, if he said: 'So-and-so gets a thousand dirhams from my third [of the estate]', this is a will even if he did not mention death in it. And if he said: 'So-and-so gets a thousand dirhams from a third of my wealth', or he said 'from half of my wealth', or he said 'from a quarter of my wealth', then it is invalid.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It establishes the general principle for distinguishing between a will (wasiyya) and a gift (hibah) when a person makes a statement during lifetime that could be interpreted as either. The key determinant is whether the statement is explicitly tied to death: either by mentioning death directly, by being placed in the context of discussing wills, or by linking the transfer to after death. If none of these conditions are present, the statement is treated as a gift (hibah) and not a will. The author emphasizes that this rule applies equally in health and illness. The passage then reports a narration from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, who transmits from Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa, providing specific examples: if a person says 'if an event happens to me' (which implies death), it is a will; if he says 'from my third' (even without mentioning death), it is also a will. However, if he uses indefinite fractions like 'from a third of my wealth', 'from half', or 'from a quarter', the statement is invalid as a will because it creates ambiguity about the portion. This teaches that specificity is required for a valid bequest.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A testamentary disposition that takes effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.
هبة (hibah): A gift inter vivos, effective immediately upon offer and acceptance.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, which is the maximum that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person says in health 'So-and-so gets a thousand dirhams from my third' without mentioning death, what is the ruling?
A) It is a valid will (wasiyya).
B) It is a gift (hibah).
C) It is invalid because 'from my third' is ambiguous.
D) It depends on whether the person recovers from illness.

Key Takeaway
A statement is a will only if it explicitly references death, is placed in the context of wills, or uses the specific phrase 'from my third'; indefinite fractions invalidate the bequest.

Wording of Wills: The Context of Dhikr al-Wasiyya
Rulings on wording of wills

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a statement made by a sick person is only a valid will if said in the context of mentioning a will, and apply it to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A sick person's statement about giving money is a will only if made in the context of a will (dhikr al-wasiyya).

In Hanafi fiqh, not every statement by a sick person about disposing of wealth becomes a valid bequest. The crucial factor is whether the statement was made in the context of a will (ذكر الوصية). This lesson examines several cases from later Hanafi works (al-Khaniyya, Fatawa al-Layth) that clarify how wording and context determine the validity and extent of a wasiyyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the speaker's statement
Read the phrase uttered by the sick or dying person. Note the exact words and whether an amount is specified.
For example, 'Take out a thousand dirhams' vs. 'I have already willed one-third of my wealth.'
2
Determine if the statement was made in the context of a will
Check whether the conversation or situation indicates that the person is explicitly making a will (dhikr al-wasiyya). Without this context, the statement has no effect as a bequest.
The text says 'إلا أن يكون عند ذكر الوصية' – unless it is at the time of mentioning a will.
3
Clarify the amount if ambiguous
If the statement is a valid will but the amount is unclear, Hanafi rulings provide default interpretations. For example, 'I have willed two thousand' without specifying from which portion results in only one-third of the estate being used, and the stated amount may be reduced proportionally.
In the case where a man said 'I have already willed one-third of my wealth,' he gives half of that one-third (i.e., one-sixth) to the poor because the phrase is interpreted as a past will.
4
Apply the rule to each case in the passage
Work through the examples from Fatawa al-Layth and al-Khaniyya, verifying the outcome based on the presence or absence of dhikr al-wasiyya.
Key example: A sick person says 'Take out a thousand dirhams' – valid only if said in the context of a will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية : قال ذلك في صحته أو مرضه إلا أن يكون عند ذكر الوصية. وفي فتاوى الليث : مريض قال أخرجوا ألف درهم من مالي أو قال أخرجوا ألف درهم ولم يزد على هذا ثم مات فإن قال ذلك في ذكر الوصية جاز. وفي الخانية، ويصرف إلى الفقراء رجل حضرته الوفاة فقال له رجل ألا توصي فقال قد أوصيت بثلث مالي ولم يزد عليه حتى مات يدفع كل السدس للفقراء. وفي الخانية : مريض قالوا له لم لا توصي فقال قد أوصيت ألفان فيتصدق بألف على المساكين ولم يزد على ذلك حتى مات فإذا . ثلث بأن يخرج من مالي ثلث ماله ألفان. قال الشيخ الإمام أبو القاسم يتصدق بالألف ولو قال المريض أوصيت أن يخرج ثلث مالي ولم يزد عليه قال بتصدق بجميع الثلث على الفقراء
In al-Khaniyya: He said that in his health or illness, except when it is in the context of mentioning a will. In Fatawa al-Layth: A sick person said: 'Take out a thousand dirhams from my wealth' or said: 'Take out a thousand dirhams' and added nothing more, then died. If he said that in the context of mentioning a will, it is permitted. In al-Khaniyya: And it is given to the poor. A man was present at death and another said to him: 'Will you not make a will?' He said: 'I have already made a will with one-third of my wealth' and added nothing until he died. He gives half of the (one-) sixth to the poor. In al-Khaniyya: A sick person was told: 'Why do you not make a will?' He said: 'I have already made a will of two thousand' so one thousand is given in charity to the needy, and he added nothing to that until he died. Then one-third: meaning one-third of his property is taken out, i.e., two thousand. The Shaykh Imam Abu al-Qasim said: He gives charity with the one thousand. And if the sick person said: 'I have willed that one-third of my wealth be taken out' and added nothing, he said: He gives charity with the entire third to the poor.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings from various sources (al-Khaniyya, Fatawa al-Layth) regarding the wording used in wills and their effects. The first ruling states that whether a statement is made in health or illness, it is treated as a will if it is explicitly made in the context of a will. The second ruling from Fatawa al-Layth gives an example: if a sick person says 'take out a thousand dirhams from my wealth' or just 'take out a thousand dirhams' without specifying, and then dies, it is only valid if said in the context of making a will; otherwise, it is not a valid bequest. The third ruling: a dying man says 'I have already willed one-third of my wealth' and dies without further detail; the executor gives half of that one-third (i.e., one-sixth) to the poor because the phrase is ambiguous. The fourth ruling: a sick person says 'I have already willed two thousand' (possibly meaning in a past will); it is understood that he meant a new will, so one thousand is given in charity. The shaykh clarifies that if he says 'I have willed that my third be taken out', the entire third goes to charity. These cases illustrate that ambiguous or incomplete statements may result in only part of the intended amount being executed, unless the context clarifies the intention.

Key Terms
ذكر الوصية (dhikr al-wasiyya): The context of explicitly discussing or mentioning a will, which makes a statement a bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fatawa al-Layth, if a sick person says 'Take out a thousand dirhams' without more, and dies, when is it valid?
A) If he said it in the context of mentioning a will.
B) Always valid because he is sick.
C) Valid only if he specified 'from my third'.
D) Never valid because it is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a sick or dying person's statement about disposing of wealth is a valid will only if made in the explicit context of a will (dhikr al-wasiyya).

Effect of Recovery on a Conditional Will: Qiyas vs. Istihsan
Rulings on conditional wills and recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the qiyas and istihsan positions on whether a conditional will is revived after recovery and reaffirmation, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A will conditional on death from a specific illness is void upon recovery, but Istihsan revives it if the testator reaffirms it in a subsequent illness.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding wills made during terminal illness. While qiyas (analogy) dictates that a conditional will lapses upon recovery, Imam Muhammad employs istihsan (juridical preference) to uphold the will when the testator later reaffirms it. Understanding this tension between strict analogy and equitable preference is essential for correctly applying Hanafi estate law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Conditional Will Act
The testator says: 'If I die from this illness, my slave is free' etc. This makes the will conditional upon death from that specific illness.
The condition is tied to a particular illness, not death in general.
2
State the Qiyas Ruling
Under qiyas, when the testator recovers, the condition (death from that illness) fails, so the will becomes void automatically.
This is the default position attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
State the Istihsan Position
Imam Muhammad rules by istihsan that if the testator later falls ill again and expressly reaffirms the earlier will, the will is valid and beneficiaries share in the one-third.
The reaffirmation shows renewed intent, overriding the previous lapse.
4
Analyze the Basis of Istihsan
Istihsan is preferred because it upholds the testator's clear intention (reaffirmation) over a strict application of conditionality that would defeat that intention.
Imam Muhammad states: 'لكنا نستحسن فنجيز ذلك' – we do istihsan and validate it.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi Ruling
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Imam Muhammad's istihsan: recovery voids the will unless the testator explicitly reaffirms it in a subsequent illness.
The text adopts this as the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المنتقى : إذا قال إن مت من مرضي هذا فأمتي هذه حرة وما كان في يدها فهو عليها صدقة قال : أرى ذلك جائزاً على وجه الصدقة وما كان في يدها يوم مات وعليه البينة أن هذا كان في يدها يوم مات، ولو قال إن مت من مرضي هذا فغلماني أحرار ويعطى فلان من مالي كذا وكذا ويحج عني ثم برأ مرضه ثم مرض ثانياً وقال للشهود الذين أشهدهم على الوصية الأولى أو لغيرهم اشهدوا أني على الوصية الأولى قال محمد أما في القياس هذا باطل لأنه قد بطلت وصيته الأولى حين صح من مرضه ذلك لكنا نستحسن فنجيز ذلك منه ويتحاصون في الثلث، وعلى هذا القياس والاستحسان إذا قال أوصيت لعبد ابنه بمائة درهم وللمساكين بمائة درهم ثم قال إن مت من مرضي هذا فغلماني أحرار ثم برأ ثم مرض ثانياً. ولو قال إن لم أبرأ من مرضي وزاد في فتاوي الفضلي أو قال بالفارسية الدين الدين يتمارى من أبدأ يأرين يتمارى ممن مر فحينئذ إذا برأ تبطل وصيته. وفي الظهيرية ومجموع النوازل: رجل قال لآخر في وصيته بالفارسية يتمارى دار في ربدان مرابصين من فقد جعله وصياً في تركته، وكذا لو قال معدهم وممر يأمرهم وما يجري مجراه. ولو قال المريض عمر كان من وريد من تحول مات أو قال مرور بدان من أصابع فمات قال : يصير وصية امرأة أوصت بأشياء وقال في لسان أماً وكان بها هندان قال هذه الوصية وماذا يعطي قال : هذه هل تصح من وصية لمن ليس هو من جملة أربابها والتقدير في هذا ذلك لما يخاطبه بذلك يعطى مالها أقرباؤها وقد يبطل اسم التذكرة الخانية : مريض أوصى بوصايا يأثم برأ من مرضه ذلك وعاش سنين ذلك حر من بعد أن ثم قال ثم مرض فوصاياه ثابتة إن لم يقل إن مت من مرضي هذا أو قال إن لم أبرأ من مرضي هذا فقد أوصيت بكذا أو قال بالفارسية الدمن ارين سماري غير من حينئذ إذا برأ بطلت وصيته
In al-Muntaqa: If he said 'If I die from this illness of mine, then my female slave is free and whatever is in her hand is charity for her', he said: I consider that permissible as a charity. And whatever was in her hand on the day he died, with proof that it was in her hand on the day he died. And if he said 'If I die from this illness of mine, then my male slaves are free, and so-and-so is given such-and-such from my wealth, and hajj is performed for me', then he recovered from his illness, then fell ill a second time, and said to the witnesses he had appointed for the first will or to others: 'Bear witness that I am upon the first will' — Muhammad said: In qiyas this is invalid because his first will became void when he recovered from that illness, but we do istihsan and validate it from him, and they share proportionally in the one-third. And upon this qiyas and istihsan, if he said 'I have willed to the slave of his son a hundred dirhams, and to the poor a hundred dirhams', then said 'If I die from this illness, my male slaves are free', then he recovered, then fell ill a second time. And if he said 'If I do not recover from my illness' — and he added in Fatawa al-Fadli or he said in Persian 'al-din al-din yatamara min abda yarayn yatamara min man mar' — then when he recovers, his will is void. In al-Zahiriyya and Majmu' al-Nawazil: A man said to another in his will in Persian 'yatamara dar fi ribdan marabasin min faqad ja'alahu wasiyyan fi tarikatihi', and similarly if he said 'ma'dahum wa marr ya'muruhum' and what runs in that course. And if the sick person said 'umar kana min warid min tahawwul mat' or said 'murur badin min asabi' f'mat', he said: It becomes a will. A woman made a will regarding things and said in the tongue 'amma' and she had Hindan. He said: This will — and what should she give? He said: Is this valid as a will for one who is not among its owners? The estimation in this is that since she addressed him with that, her wealth is given to her relatives, and the name of remembrance may be void. Al-Khaniyya: A sick person made wills, then he recovered from that illness and lived for years, that (slave) is free after that. Then he fell ill, and his wills remain valid if he did not say 'If I die from this illness' or said 'If I do not recover from this illness, I have willed such-and-such' or he said in Persian 'al-daman arin samari ghayr min' then when he recovers, his will is void.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings on the effect of recovery from illness on a will made during that illness. The main rule is that a will made during a terminal illness is conditional upon death from that illness. If the person recovers, the will becomes void (batalat) because the condition is no longer met. However, if they later fall ill again and explicitly reaffirm the earlier will, Imam Muhammad rules by istihsan (juridical preference) that the earlier will is revived and the beneficiaries share in the one-third. By qiyas, the will would be void and need to be made anew, but istihsan takes precedence. The text also discusses various Persian formulations that indicate a conditional will. The ruling from al-Zahiriyya discusses appointment of an executor (wasi) using Persian terms. The final ruling from al-Khaniyya clarifies that if a person recovers and lives for years, and then falls ill again, the wills remain valid only if they were not made conditional on death from the first illness or on non-recovery. The key lesson is that the validity of a conditional will depends on the condition being fulfilled; recovery nullifies it unless the testator explicitly reaffirms it.

Key Terms
برأ (bari'a): Recovery from the illness during which the will was made.
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if a person makes a will during illness, recovers, then falls ill again and tells witnesses he is upon the first will, what is the ruling?
A) The will is void by qiyas but valid by istihsan.
B) The will is void because the first illness ended.
C) The will is valid only if he repeats the exact words.
D) The will is valid only for the one-third.

Key Takeaway
A will conditional on death from a specific illness lapses upon recovery; but if the testator reaffirms it during a subsequent illness, the Hanafi school enforces it by istihsan.

General Discharge of Debtors Without Specification is Not a Valid Will
Ruling that a general discharge of debtors without naming them is not a valid will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of specific identification in a will for debt forgiveness and determine the validity of a general discharge statement.

Core Idea
A will that says 'I discharge my debtors' without naming them does not effect a discharge; specificity is required.

The first ruling in our passage addresses a common scenario: a person writes in his will that all his debtors are discharged, without naming them or intending any specific individual. The author rules that such a general statement does not constitute a valid will, because the debtors remain unknown. This lesson will unpack the condition of specificity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is a statement of debt forgiveness (ibra) included in a will.
2
Identify the missing element
The testator did not name the debtors and did not intend any of them in his heart. This lack of specification is the key issue.
3
Apply the ruling
Since the debtors are not identified, the statement is not a valid will; the debtors are not discharged. The heirs must collect the debts.
The ruling is from Abu al-Qasim citing Ibn Muqatil from our companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال أبرأت غرماني ولم يسمهم ولم ينو أحداً منهم بقلبه قال أبو القاسم: روى ابن مقاتل أصحابنا أنهم لا يبرؤون . رجل له دين على رجل فقال المديون إذا مت فأنت بريء من ذلك الدين قال أبو القاسم: يجوز ويكون وصية من الطالب للمطلوب. وفي النوازل سئل عن رجل كان له على رجل دين فقال له إذا مت فأنت بريء من ذلك الدين قال : يجوز وتكون وصية من الطالب للمطلوب إذا مات وإذا قال إن مت برئ من ذلك الدين قال : لا يبرأ وهو مخاطرة. وهو بمنزلة قوله إن دخلت الدار فأنت بريء مما عليك . وفي المنتقى : إذا قال الرجل ضعوا ثلثي حيث أمر الله تعالى يرد إلى الورثة. وفي الخلاصة: ولو قال ثلث مالي حيثما يرى الناس أو حيثما يرى المسلمون قيل في عرفنا ليست بوصية. وفي العيون: إذا قال انظروا إلى كل ما يجوز لي أن يوصى به فأعطوه فهذا على الثلث ولو قال انظروا ما يجوز لي أن أوصى به فأعطوه فالأمر إلى الورثة لأنه يجوز أن يوصي بدرهم وبأكثر. وقوله ما يجوز لي كذا ذكرهما ههنا ومراده إذا كانت الورثة كباراً ،كلهم أما إذا كان فيهم صغير أو من في معناه يجعل في حقه كان الموصي أوصى بدرهم لا غير لأنه هو المتيقن. وسئل أبو نصر عمن ادفعوا هذه الدراهم أو هذه الثياب إلى فلان ولم يقل هي له قال : إن هذا باطل لأن هذا ليس بوصية. وسئل أبو نصر الدبوسي عمن قال في وصيته ثلث مالي وقف ولم يزد على هذا قال : إن كان ماله نقداً يعني دراهم أو دنانير وما أشبه ذلك فهذا القول منه باطل وصار كقوله هذه الدراهم وقف، وإن كان ماله ضياعاً ونحوه صار وقفاً على الفقراء. وفي الظهيرية : وقد قيل الفتوى على أنه لا يجوز ما لم يبين جهة الوقف ولو أوصى رجل أن ما وجد مكتوباً من وصية والدي ولم أكن نفذتها تنفذ أو أقر بذلك على نفسه إقراراً في مرضه قالوا: هذه إن صدقته الورثة بتصديقهم، وإن كذبوه كان من الثلث بخلاف الدين. وفي الخانية : بخلاف الدين الذي لا طالب له إلا الله تعالى وكان حكمه حكم الزكاة والكفارات. وسئل محمد بن مقاتل عمن أوصى أن يعطي للناس ألف درهم قال : الوصية باطلة، ولو قال تصدقوا بألف درهم فهو جائز ويعطى للفقراء. وفي الخلاصة : لو قال لعبده أنت الله لا يعتق وقال محمد: الوصية جائزة وتصرف إلى وجوه البر وفي الخانية وفي مسألة العتق إن أراد به العتق عتق، وإن أراد به أنه الله لا يلزمه شيء والوصية تارة تكون بالألفاظ وتارة تكون بالإشارة المفهمة . قال في فتاوى أبي الليث : مريض أوصى وهو لا يقدر على الكلام لضعفه فأشار برأسه يعلم منه أنه يعتمد قال ابن مقاتل : تجوز وصيته عندي ولا تجوز عند أصحابنا، وكان الفقيه أبر الليث يقول : إذا فهم منه الإشارة يجوز. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : إذا كتب وصيته ثم قال أنفذوا وما في هذا الكتاب تنفذ وصيته ؛ هكذا ذكر في كتاب الشهادات قال الشيخ الإمام أبو وصية
And if he said: 'I have discharged my debtors' but did not name them and did not intend any of them in his heart, Abu al-Qasim said: Ibn Muqatil narrated from our companions that they are not discharged. A man had a debt upon another, and the debtor said: 'When I die, you are free from that debt.' Abu al-Qasim said: It is permitted and it becomes a will from the creditor for the debtor. In al-Nawazil, he was asked about a man who had a debt upon another and he said to him: 'When I die, you are free from that debt.' He said: It is permitted and it becomes a will from the creditor for the debtor when he dies. And if he said: 'If I die, you are free from that debt,' he said: He is not discharged, and it is a gamble (mukhatara). It is like his saying: 'If you enter the house, you are free from what you owe.' In al-Muntaqa: If a man said: 'Place my third where Allah commands,' it is returned to the heirs. In al-Khulasa: And if he said: 'My third is placed wherever people see or wherever Muslims see,' it is said in our custom that it is not a will. In al-‘Uyun: If he said: 'Look at everything permissible for me to bequeath and give it to him,' this is upon the third. And if he said: 'Look at what is permissible for me to bequeath and give it to him,' the matter is up to the heirs because it is permissible for him to will a dirham or more. And his saying 'what is permissible for me' — both were mentioned here; his intent is if all heirs are adults, but if there is a minor or similar among them, it is made in his case as if the testator willed one dirham only, because that is certain. And Abu Nasr was asked about one who said: 'Give these dirhams or these clothes to so-and-so' and did not say 'they are for him.' He said: This is invalid because it is not a will. And Abu Nasr al-Dabusi was asked about one who said in his will: 'My third is a waqf' and added nothing. He said: If his wealth is cash, i.e., dirhams or dinars and the like, then this statement of his is invalid and becomes like his saying 'these dirhams are a waqf'; and if his wealth is estates and the like, it becomes a waqf for the poor. In al-Zahiriyya: It has been said that the fatwa is that it is not permitted unless he specifies the direction of the waqf. And if a man willed that whatever is found written as the will of my father which I did not execute be executed, or he acknowledged that against himself in his illness, they said: This, if the heirs confirm it, it is by their confirmation, and if they deny it, it is from the third, unlike debt. In al-Khaniyya: Unlike a debt for which there is no claimant except Allah Almighty, and its ruling is like that of zakat and expiations. And Muhammad ibn Muqatil was asked about one who willed to give people a thousand dirhams. He said: The will is invalid. But if he said: 'Give charity with a thousand dirhams,' it is valid and given to the poor. In al-Khulasa: If he said to his slave: 'You are Allah,' he does not become free. And Muhammad said: The will is valid and it is given to good causes. And in al-Khaniyya, in the case of manumission: if he intended by it manumission, he is free; if he intended that he is Allah, nothing is binding upon him. And will sometimes is by words and sometimes by meaningful indication. It is stated in Fatawa Abi al-Layth: A sick person made a will while unable to speak due to weakness, and he indicated with his head, and it is known from him that he intended. Ibn Muqatil said: His will is valid according to me, but not according to our companions. And al-Faqih Abi al-Layth used to say: If the indication is understood from him, it is valid. And in Fatawa Abi al-Layth: If he wrote his will and then said: 'Execute, and whatever is in this book, execute my will.' Thus it is mentioned in the Book of Testimonies. The Shaykh Imam Abu... will
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a collection of miscellaneous rulings from various sources concerning the validity of different statements as wills. The first ruling clarifies that a general statement 'I have discharged my debtors' without naming them or specific intent does not effect a discharge; it is not a valid will. The second ruling addresses debt forgiveness linked to death: if the debtor says 'when I die, you are free from the debt,' it is a valid will from the creditor, i.e., the creditor is considered to have made a bequest forgiving the debt. But if the debtor says 'if I die, you are free,' it is considered a gamble (mukhatara) and invalid because it is conditional. The next ruling from al-Muntaqa: if someone says 'place my third where Allah commands' without specifying a charitable cause, the money is returned to the heirs because the direction is too vague. Similarly, saying 'wherever people see' is not a valid will. The 'Uyun ruling distinguishes between two similar phrases: 'look at everything permissible for me to bequeath' limits the bequest to one-third, while 'look at what is permissible for me to bequeath' gives discretion to the heirs, who may give less if they wish, unless there is a minor heir, in which case a minimum of one dirham is presumed. Abu Nasr rules that saying 'give these dirhams to so-and-so' without saying 'they are for him' does not constitute a will because ownership is not transferred. Al-Dabusi's ruling on making one-third a waqf without specifying the beneficiary: if the wealth is cash, the statement is invalid because cash waqf is not recognized in that context; if it is land, it becomes a waqf for the poor. The written father's will: if a person says to execute whatever is found written as his father's will, it is only binding if the heirs confirm; otherwise, it is from the one-third. The final rulings discuss the validity of a will by indication (ishara) and by writing. There is a difference of opinion: Ibn Muqatil allows indication if understood, while other Hanafi companions do not. Abu al-Layth accepts it. Writing a will and then instructing its execution is valid.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Discharge of a debt, which can be made as a will.
غرمان (ghurman): Debtors, plural of gharim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, what is the ruling if a testator says 'I have discharged my debtors' without naming anyone?
A) The debtors are discharged because the intention is clear.
B) The debtors are not discharged because the statement is too vague.
C) The debtors are discharged but only if the heir agrees.
D) The will is valid but the debts are not forgiven.

Key Takeaway
A will that forgives debts must specifically identify the debtors; a general discharge is ineffective.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
