لأن شيئاً من وصيته لا يبطل بعد إجازة الورثة فصار الثلث على أربعة والعبد كله على اثني عشر سهماً يسلم لصاحب الرقبة سهم من ثلاثة وذلك جزء من اثني عشر جزءاً ويباع الباقي بأحد عشر جزءاً من الألف وقيل المذكور في الكتاب قول الكل، وأن أجازوا ورضي بذلك صاحب البيع يضرب كل واحد بكمال وصيته فيقسم نصفين : نصفه لصاحب الرقبة ونصفه يباع من الآخر فيكون ثمنه بين الورثة لأن حقيهما قد استويا عند إجازة الورثة فتساويا ضرباً واستحقاقاً. وقيل عند أبي حنيفة على أربعة أوجه والوجه الثاني : لو أوصى أن يباع العبد من رجل بألف وأوصى بجميع ماله لآخر فهذا كالمسألة الأولى في قول أبي حنيفة إلا أن صاحب الجميع يأخذ سدس الألف الورثة من جملة الثمن مع أخذه من سدس الرقبة، وفي المسألة الأولى ليس له من الثمن شيء لأنه أوصى له بالمال هنا والثمن لمالك الرقبة فيجوز تنفيذ ثمنه في الثمن وهناك أوصى له بالعين وهي الرقبة والثمن غير فلا يمكن تكميل وصيته من الثمن، وإن أجازوا بيع نصف العبد ثم أخذ صاحب الجميع ثمنه فلا شيء للورثة. وقيل عند أبي حنيفة إن لم يجيزوا فمن اثني عشر كما في المسألة الأولى فهما مرا على أصلهما. وعلى قول أبي يوسف ينبغي أن يباع العبد كله من الموصى له بالبيع بألف ثم يعطي الموصي له بالمال ثلث الثمن لأن هذا أمكن تنفيذ الوصيتين لاختلاف محل حقهما لأن حق أحدهما في الرقبة وحق الآخر في مطلق المال والثمن مال كالرقبة فتنفذ كلاهما لهما لما مات الموصى جاء أولاً تنفيذ الوصية ومحل ذلك ماله والرقبة ماله فتنفذ فيها ولا يجوز التأخير إذ في التأخير توهم الإبطال بهلاك الموصى به والوجه الثالث : لو أوصى أن يباع من فلان بألف وأوصى بثلث ماله لآخر فقول محمد كقول أبي حنيفة في هذا يأخذ صاحب الثلث جزءاً من اثني عشر جزءاً من الرقبة ويباع الباقي من الموصى له بالبيع يأخذ أحد عشر جزءاً من الألف إلا أن صاحب الثلث يأخذ من الثمن تمام الثلث ثم موصى له بثلث ماله والثمن ماله. وعند أبي يوسف يباع الكل من الموصى له بالبيع ويعطي من الثلث الثمن إلى صاحبه ولو أوصى بالعبد إلى رجل وقيمته ألف وأوصى أن يباع من آخر بمائة درهم فعند أبي حنيفة نصف السدس من العبد للموصى له به ويباع الباقي من صاحب البيع من ثلث قيمة العبد فيسلم للورثة لأن عنده يصير الثلث على أربعة أسهم لصاحب الرقبة ربع السدس وهو جزء من اثني عشر جزءاً ويباع الباقي من صاحب البيع بثلثي قيمة العبد بثلث قيمته وذلك ستمائة وستة وستون وثلثان فيسلم ذلك للورثة لأنهما وصيتان وصية بالبيع ووصية بالمحاباة في الثمن لأن الوصية بالمحاباة إنما تنفذ من الثلث فينظر إلى ما بقي من الثلث بعد ما أخذ صاحب الرقبة وذلك ثلاثة أجزاء فيسلم ذلك المقدار له وما بقي وهو ثلث المال حق الورثة وعنده الوصية بالمحاباة مقدمة على سائر الوصايا ولكن محاباة منفذة تثبت في ضمن عقد لازم لا يملك الموصي الرجوع عنها وهذا وصية بمحاباة غير منفذة . وعند محمد لصاحب الرقبة سدس العبد ويباع الباقي بثلثي الألف لأن حقهما في الثلث على السواء فيضرب كل واحد منهما بجميع حقه فيكون الثلث بينهما نصفين نصفه لصاحب الرقبة نصفه يباع من صاحب البيع بثلثي القيمة
Because nothing from his bequest is invalidated after the heirs' permission, so the one-third becomes [divided] into four, and the entire slave into twelve shares: the owner of the slave's corpus receives one share out of three, which is one part out of twelve, and the remainder is sold for eleven parts out of a thousand. It is said that what is mentioned in the book is the statement of all. And if they [the heirs] permit and the buyer agrees, each [legatee] enters with his full bequest, and it is divided into two halves: half for the owner of the slave's corpus and half is sold to the other, so its price goes to the heirs because their rights become equal upon the heirs' permission, so they become equal in entering and entitlement. And it is said according to Abu Hanifa that there are four aspects. The second aspect: If he bequeaths that the slave be sold to a man for a thousand and bequeaths all his property to another, this is like the first case according to Abu Hanifa, except that the recipient of all takes one-sixth of the thousand from the total price along with his taking from one-sixth of the slave's corpus. In the first case, he receives nothing from the price because he was bequeathed the property here, and the price belongs to the owner of the corpus, so executing his [bequest] in the price is permissible; whereas there he was bequeathed the specific thing, which is the corpus, and the price is different, so it is not possible to complete his bequest from the price. And if they permit the sale of half the slave, then the recipient of all takes his price, so nothing remains for the heirs. And it is said according to Abu Hanifa that if they do not permit, then from twelve as in the first case, both revert to their respective positions. According to Abu Yusuf, the entire slave should be sold to the person bequeathed the sale for a thousand, then he gives the recipient of the property one-third of the price, because this makes it more possible to execute both bequests due to the difference in the locus of their rights: one's right is in the slave's corpus and the other's right is in absolute property, and the price is property like the corpus, so both bequests are executed. When the testator died, the execution of the bequest comes first, and its locus is his property, and the slave's corpus is his property, so it is executed therein, and delay is not permissible because delay entails the possibility of nullification due to destruction of the bequest. The third aspect: If he bequeaths that [the slave] be sold to so-and-so for a thousand and bequeaths one-third of his property to another: the statement of Muhammad is like that of Abu Hanifa in this: the recipient of one-third takes one part out of twelve from the slave's corpus, and the remainder is sold to the person bequeathed the sale, who takes eleven parts of the thousand, except that the recipient of one-third takes from the price to complete one-third, then he is the recipient of one-third of his property, and the price is his property. According to Abu Yusuf, the entire slave is sold to the person bequeathed the sale, and he gives from the one-third of the price to his companion. And if he bequeaths the slave to a man—its value one thousand—and bequeaths that it be sold to another for one hundred dirhams: according to Abu Hanifa, half of one-sixth of the slave is for the person bequeathed the slave, and the remainder is sold to the buyer from one-third of the slave's value, and it remains for the heirs. Because in his view, the one-third becomes into four shares: the owner of the slave's corpus gets one-quarter of one-sixth, which is one part out of twelve, and the remainder is sold to the buyer for two-thirds of the slave's value minus one-third of its value, which is six hundred sixty-six and two-thirds, and that remains for the heirs. Because there are two bequests: a bequest of sale and a bequest of premium (muhabah) in the price. The bequest of premium is only executed from the one-third. So one looks at what remains of the one-third after the owner of the corpus takes, which is three parts; that amount is given to him, and what remains—which is one-third of the property—is the right of the heirs. In his view, the bequest of premium takes precedence over other bequests, but a executed premium is established within a binding contract from which the testator cannot retract, whereas this is a non-executed bequest of premium. According to Muhammad: one-sixth of the slave is for the owner of the slave's corpus, and the remainder is sold for two-thirds of the thousand, because their rights in the one-third are equal; each enters with all of his right, so the one-third is between them in halves: half for the owner of the corpus, half is sold to the buyer for two-thirds of the value.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute covering several scenarios where a testator combines two bequests: one involving the sale of a slave at a specific price, and another bequest of a portion of his property. The core issue is how to allocate the one-third of the estate (the maximum that can be bequeathed) when there are competing claims. The text describes three main subcases:

1. **Second Aspect (al-wajh al-thani)**: The testator bequeaths that a slave be sold to a person for 1,000 dirhams, and also bequeaths all his property to another. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ. In Abu Hanifa’s view, if the heirs permit, the proceeds of the sale are split: the recipient of all property takes a share from both the slave's corpus and the price. Without the heirs' permission, the calculation is from twelve. Abu Yusuf holds that the entire slave should be sold, and the recipient of all property gets one-third of the price, because both bequests can be executed simultaneously due to the different loci of rights.

2. **Third Aspect**: The testator bequeaths the slave's sale for 1,000 and bequeaths one-third of his property to another. Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa: the recipient of one-third takes a fraction from the slave's corpus, and the rest is sold. Abu Yusuf again sells the whole slave and gives the one-third from the price.

3. **Case of bequest of the slave (value 1,000) and bequest of its sale for only 100 dirhams**: This involves a premium (muhabah) because the sale price is below market value. Abu Hanifa treats this as two bequests: one for the slave's corpus and one for the premium. He calculates that the owner of the corpus gets half of one-sixth of the slave, and the remainder is sold, with the premium coming from the one-third. Muhammad differs: the owner gets one-sixth of the slave, and the remainder is sold for two-thirds of the value, dividing the one-third equally between the two legatees.

The passage illustrates the Hanafi principle that competing bequests are resolved by proportional allocation from the one-third, with disagreements on whether certain bequests (like a sale order) can be partially executed or must be fully implemented when possible. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as this is a standard commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Key Terms
وصية بالمحاباة (wasiyyah bi al-muhabah): A bequest of a premium (discount) in a sale, where the testator instructs that a slave be sold below market value, and the difference is treated as a bequest.
الرقبة (al-raqabah): The slave's corpus (the slave itself as a capital asset), distinguished from its price or value.
الوصية بالبيع (al-wasiyyah bi al-bay'): A bequest that a specific item (here a slave) be sold to a named person at a fixed price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second aspect described by the passage, what does Abu Hanifa rule regarding the bequest of all property combined with a bequest to sell a slave for 1000, when the heirs do not permit?
A) The entire slave is sold and the legatee of all property takes from the price.
B) The legatee of all property takes one-sixth from both the slave and the price from the one-third.
C) The slave is divided into twelve shares; the legatee takes one share and the rest is sold.
D) The bequest of sale is nullified and the legatee of property takes the entire slave.

Key Takeaway
When competing bequests involve a specific sale instruction and a property bequest, the Hanafi school splits: Abu Hanifa allocates proportionally from both the specific asset and the price, while Abu Yusuf sells the asset fully to satisfy the sale.

The 'Arusa Case: Resolving Competing Bequests from the One-Third
Intra-Hanafi dispute on apportioning one-third for competing bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi imams' methods for apportioning the one-third when a testator bequeaths all property and a slave at a discount, and identify the practical difference in outcomes.

Core Idea
When bequests exceed one-third, the three Hanafi imams differ in calculation—each reflects a valid juristic method.

The arusa case—so named for the elegance of its derivation—presents a puzzle: a testator leaves all his property to one person and orders his slave (worth 1,000 dirhams) sold to another for only 100. The heirs refuse to approve. How is the estate divided from the permissible one-third? Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani each offer a systematic solution. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the practical differences that result.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Recognize that we have two bequests: a bequest of all property (the entire estate, including the slave) and a bequest to sell the slave at a discount (i.e., premium of 900). The heirs do not consent, so only one-third of the estate can be used for bequests.
The estate includes the slave worth 1,000 and other property (unspecified). The bequest of 'all property' means everything goes to one legatee, but the sale instruction is also a bequest.
2
Understand each imam's principle
Abu Hanifa treats the property bequest as giving the legatee a direct share of the slave's corpus. Muhammad splits the one-third equally between the two legatees. Abu Yusuf treats the premium as a separate bequest and uses a share-based method.
These different starting points lead to different final distributions.
3
Walk through Muhammad's derivation
Follow the text's detailed explanation: the one-third is split in half; one-sixth of the slave goes to the property legatee. The remaining five-sixths are sold to the buyer, with adjustments for the nullification of part of the premium.
The nullification occurs because the property legatee's share of the slave takes priority over the sale bequest.
4
Note Abu Yusuf's approach
He treats the premium (900) and the sale price (100) as two separate bequests. He divides the one-third into 19 shares (10 for property, 9 for premium) and then sells the entire slave for 48/57 of its value.
This method yields a different fraction: the property legatee gets 10/57 of the slave's value.
5
Compare outcomes
Under Abu Hanifa, the property legatee gets one-third of the slave; under Muhammad, one-sixth; under Abu Yusuf, a portion worth 10/57. The heirs receive different amounts as well. This thamarah al-khilaf highlights the practical impact of the juristic methods.
The text notes Muhammad's derivation is 'on its weakness' (على ضعف ذلك), suggesting it is less preferred, but no definitive tarjih is given.

أربعمائة أو سبعة عشر سهماً من قيمة العبد يأخذ الموصى له بالمال خمسة أسهم وربع سهم من من الثمن تمام وصيته ومائتان وثمانية وسبعون للورثة. وعند محمد سدس العبد للموصى له بالمال ويباع خمسة أسداسه الآخر سبعة وعشرين من اثنين وأربعين من قيمة العبد سهم من له بالمال تمام وصيته وثمانية وعشرون للورثة وهذه المسألة ملقبة بالعروس لحسن تخريجها ووضوح طريقها. أما تخريجها لمحمد أن حق الموصي في الثلث على السواء سدسه وذلك مائة وخمسون من تسعمائة لأن سدس الرقبة صار مستحقاً للموصى له بالمال بوصيته فبطلت فيه الوصية بالبيع والوصية بالمحاباة في ضمن الوصية بالبيع فتبطل ببطلانها ألا ترى أن الموصى له بالبيع لو قال لا If he bequeathed all his property to a man and that [a slave] be sold to another for one hundred, and the heirs do not permit, then the analogical reasoning of Abu Hanifa is that the recipient of all property takes one-third of the slave, and what remains, which is ten parts out of twelve, is sold for two hundred and one-third shares and two hundred and a quarter, four hundred, or seventeen shares of the slave's value. The recipient of the property takes five and a quarter shares from the price to complete his bequest, and two hundred and seventy-eight go to the heirs. According to Muhammad: one-sixth of the slave is for the recipient of the property, and the remaining five-sixths are sold for twenty-seven out of forty-two shares of the slave's value; the recipient of the property takes a share to complete his bequest, and twenty-eight go to the heirs. This case is called 'al-Arusa' (the bride) due to the beauty of its derivation and clarity of its method. As for Muhammad's derivation: the testator's right in the one-third is equal, so the recipient of the property gets half of the one-third, which is one-sixth of the slave, and it is sold to the other for twenty-seven out of forty-two of the slave's value. These are two bequests: a bequest of all property and a bequest of premium to the buyer of nine hundred. However, one-sixth of his bequest is nullified, which is one hundred and fifty out of nine hundred, because one-sixth of the slave's corpus became due to the recipient of the property by his bequest, so the bequest of sale and the bequest of premium within it are nullified. Do you not see that if the person bequeathed the sale said, 'I do not want to buy, I want the premium,' he would not have that. So the bequest remains on seven hundred and fifty; he enters with the one-third in this amount, and the other enters with all the property; that amount is because he took one-sixth of the property, but he enters with all the property to determine the extent of his right. So what he took from the slave's corpus, which is one-sixth, is counted against him, and he is given what remains. Thus his right becomes four shares, and the right of the buyer becomes three shares of two hundred and fifty; their total is seven, so the one-third becomes upon seven, the whole becomes twenty-one. Each share… The right of the property owner is four; he has received three and a half, which is one-sixth of the slave; half of his complete right remains. The heirs' right is in fourteen, so it appears that five-sixths of the slave are sold to the buyer for fourteen shares; one share is his complete right. We have thus executed the bequest of premium in three, so the total is upon seven, and the remainder for the heirs is four; thus the one-third and two-thirds are correct. And Muhammad derived it with caution despite its weakness. As for Abu Yusuf's derivation: the entire slave is sold to the person bequeathed the sale for forty-eight shares out of fifty-seven shares of the slave's value, because here two bequests come together: a bequest of one thousand and a bequest of premium of nine hundred. Make every hundred a share; so the right of one becomes ten and the right of the other nine; their total is nineteen shares; these are the shares of the one-third, so the total is fifty-seven. The owner of the premium gets nine shares, so the slave is sold for what remains, which is forty-eight; the property owner is given ten, and the heirs get thirty-eight; thus the one-third and two-thirds are correct. As for Abu Hanifa's derivation: there are two bequests: a bequest of one thousand and a bequest…

Commentary
This passage presents a single case known as 'al-Arusa' (the bride), involving a testator who bequeaths all his property (i.e., the entire estate) to one person, and also orders that a slave be sold to another person for only 100 dirhams, while its actual value is 1,000 dirhams. The heirs do not permit the bequest to exceed the one-third limit. The three eminent Hanafi jurists—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—propose different methods for distributing the estate.

The passage first states the 'قياس قول أبي حنيفة' (analogical reasoning of Abu Hanifa), then gives Muhammad's view, and finally provides detailed derivations (takhrij) for each. The method involves converting the bequests into shares and calculating the one-third and two-thirds. The text explains Muhammad's derivation step by step: the one-third is split equally between the two bequests (property and premium), with adjustments for the nullification of part of the premium when the property bequest takes precedence. Abu Yusuf's derivation uses a different ratio: he treats the bequest of 1,000 (the sale price) and the premium of 900 as two bequests, splitting the one-third into 19 shares, then calculating the sale of the slave for 48/57 of its value. Abu Hanifa's derivation is cut off but presumably similar.

This case is called 'al-Arusa' because of the elegance of its resolution. The commentary highlights the intra-Hanafi dispute on how to apportion the one-third when there are competing bequests of different types (absolute property vs. premium in sale). The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
العروس (al-arus): A nickname for this specific case, meaning 'the bride', due to the beauty and clarity of its derivation.
تخريج (takhrij): Juridical derivation or extraction of a ruling through reasoning, often applied to imams' independent reasoning of a case.
محاباة (muhabah): Premium or discount in a sale; the difference between the actual value and the sale price treated as a gift or bequest.

Key Takeaway
The arusa case demonstrates that when multiple bequests compete from the one-third, Hanafi imams may differ in allocation methods, but all respect the one-third limitation and provide systematic derivations.

The Al-‘Arūs Case: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Bequest Calculations
Intra-Hanafi dispute on calculating bequest shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi imams' derivation methods for the al-‘arūs case and apply the principle that both legatees share the one-third proportionally.

Core Idea
When bequests exceed one-third, all legatees equally compete within the third – the imams' methods ensure just division.

In this lesson, we examine a famous Hanafi case known as 'al-‘arūs' (the bride) for its elegant yet intricate derivation. A testator makes two bequests: all his property to one person and a sale of his slave at a heavy discount (muhabah) to another. The heirs do not consent, so both bequests are limited to one-third of the estate. The three founding Hanafi imams offer different calculation methods, all correct but varying in caution. This case illustrates how Hanafi jurists apply the one-third limit when multiple bequests compete.

Guided Path
1
Understand the case facts
Identify the two bequests: (1) all property to one legatee, (2) sale of a slave worth 1000 for 100 (i.e., 900 discount). Note that heirs do not consent, so total bequests cannot exceed one-third.
The discount (muhabah) is treated as a bequest.
2
Recall the one-third limit rule
In Hanafi law, bequests to non-heirs are limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent. Here, both bequests must fit within that one-third.
This is from the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas.
3
Identify the imams' shared principle
All three imams agree that both legatees have equal priority in the one-third. The third is divided proportionally between them according to their respective rights.
The difference is only in the arithmetic method.
4
Follow Muhammad's derivation (most cautious)
Imam Muhammad doubles the base to avoid fractions. He finds that the legatee of property gets 1/6 of the slave, and the buyer gets 27/42 of the slave's value. Work through his steps: equal shares in the third, then adjust.
He uses 42 as the base to ensure whole numbers.
5
Compare Abū Yūsuf's and Abū Ḥanīfa's methods
Abū Yūsuf treats each hundred as a share and finds the third is 19 shares, leading to 48/57 of the slave. Abū Ḥanīfa uses a 12-base and accounts for the invalid portion of the muhabah bequest. Note how each arrives at the same one-third limit.
These differences are valid ikhtilāf.

المحاباة في ثلاثة فتكون الجملة على سبعة والباقي للورثة وهو أربعة فاستقام الثلث والثلثان، ومحمد أخرجه على ضعف ذلك تحرزاً. وأما تخريج أبي يوسف أنه يباع جميع العبد من الموصى له بالبيع بثمانية وأربعين سهماً من سبعة وخمسين سهماً من قيمة العبد لأنه اجتمع ها هنا وصيتان وصية بالألف ووصية بالمحاباة بتسعمائة فاجعل كل مائة سهماً فيصير حق أحدهما عشر وحق الآخر تسعة فتكون جملته تسعة عشر سهماً فهذا سهام الثلث فتكون الجملة سبعة وخمسين لصاحب المحاباة تسعة أسهم فيباع العبد بما بقي وذلك ثمانية وأربعون فيعطى لصاحب المال عشرة وللورثة ثمانية وثلاثين فاستقام الثلث والثلثان . وأما تخريج أبي حنيفة وهو أن هنا وصيتين وصية بالألف ووصية بالمحاباة تسعمائة أن وصية الألف فيما زاد على الثلث تبطل ضرباً واستحقاقاً عند عدم إجازة الورثة فبقي حقه في ثلث الألف ويبطل من وصية المحاباة وذلك خمسة وسبعون لأنه بطل الوصية بالبيع في نصف سدس الرقبة لاستحقاق الموصى بالمال لما بينا في حقه في ثمانمائة وخمسة وعشرين فخمسة وعشرون ربع ماله وقد انكسر ذلك بالأرباع وحق صاحب في ثلث الألف وذلك ثلثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث فقد انكسر بالأثلاث فاضرب ثلاثة في أربعة فيكن اثني عشر ثم اجعل كل مائة على اثني عشر كل سهم ثمانية دراهم وثلث درهم فصار حق صاحب المال أربعين سهماً وحق صاحب البيع تسعة وتسعين سهماً فيكون الثلث مائة وتسعة وثلاثين سهماً فيكون كل المال أربعمائة وسبعة عشر سهماً فحق صاحب المال أربعون سهماً وصل إليه من ذلك أربعة وثلاثون وثلاثة أرباع سهم لأنه وصل إليه من العبد نصف سدسه وذلك جزء من اثني عشر جزءاً فصار العبد على أربعمائة وأربعة عشر سهماً جزء من اثني عشر جزءاً منه يكون أربعة وثلاثين وثلاثة أرباع سهم بقي إلى تمام حقه خمسة أسهم وربع سهم وحق الورثة مائتان وثمانية وسبعون.
According to Muhammad, the owner of the slave gets one-sixth of the slave, and the remainder is sold for two-thirds of the thousand because their rights in the third are equal, so each one strikes with all his right, thus the third is divided between them in halves: half for the owner of the slave, half is sold to the buyer for two-thirds of the value. If he bequeathed all his property to a man and that another be sold for one hundred, and the heirs did not consent, then by analogy to Abu Hanifa's statement, the testator's property becomes one-third of the slave, and what remains, which is ten parts out of twelve, is sold for two hundred and one-third shares and two hundred and a quarter four hundred or seventeen shares of the slave's value; the legatee of the property takes five and a quarter shares from the price to complete his bequest, and two hundred and seventy-eight for the heirs. According to Muhammad, one-sixth of the slave is for the legatee of the property, and the other five-sixths are sold for twenty-seven out of forty-two shares of the slave's value; the legatee of the property gets his full bequest, and twenty-eight for the heirs. This case is called 'al-arus' due to the beauty of its derivation and clarity of its method. Regarding Muhammad's derivation: the testator's right in the third is equal, so the legatee of the property is given half of the third, which is one-sixth of the slave, and it is sold to the other for twenty-seven out of forty-two of the slave's value, because these are two bequests: a bequest of all property and a bequest of favor (muhabah) to the buyer of nine hundred, except that one-sixth of his bequest is invalidated, which is one hundred fifty out of nine hundred, because one-sixth of the slave became due to the legatee of the property by his bequest, so the bequest of sale and the bequest of favor within the bequest of sale are invalidated; do you not see that if the legatee of the sale said 'I do not want to buy, I want the favor,' he would not have that? So the bequest remains in seven hundred fifty, and he strikes with the third in this amount, while the other strikes with all the property and that amount, because although he took one-sixth of the property and sufficed, he strikes with all the property to ascertain the amount of his right; what he took from the slave, which is one-sixth, is accounted for, and he is given what remains. So his right became four shares, and the right of the legatee of the sale three shares, two hundred fifty, total seven, so the third becomes over seven, the total becomes twenty-one; each share is one share, so the owner of the property has four, and he has been given three and a half, which is one-sixth of the slave, remaining half of his full right, and the heirs' right is fourteen, so it appears that five-sixths of the slave are sold to the buyer for fourteen shares, one share is his full right, so we have executed the bequest of favor in three, so the total is over seven, and the remainder for the heirs is four, so the third and the two-thirds are correct. Muhammad derived it on double that out of caution. As for Abu Yusuf's derivation: all of the slave is sold to the legatee of the sale for forty-eight shares out of fifty-seven shares of the slave's value, because here two bequests have come together: a bequest of one thousand and a bequest of favor of nine hundred; make each hundred a share, so the right of one becomes ten and the other nine, total nineteen shares; these are the shares of the third, so the total becomes fifty-seven; the owner of the favor has nine shares, so the slave is sold for what remains, which is forty-eight, so the owner of the property is given ten, and the heirs thirty-eight, so the third and two-thirds are correct. As for Abu Hanifa's derivation: here there are two bequests: a bequest of one thousand and a bequest of favor of nine hundred; the bequest of one thousand, concerning what exceeds the third, is invalidated in terms of multiplication and entitlement when the heirs do not consent, so his right remains in one-third of the thousand, and from the bequest of favor, seventy-five is invalidated, because the bequest of sale was invalidated in half of one-sixth of the slave due to the entitlement of the legatee of the property, as we explained; his right is in eight hundred twenty-five, so twenty-five is a quarter of his property, and it is broken into quarters; the right of the owner of the bequest is in one-third of the thousand, that is three hundred thirty-three and one-third, it is broken into thirds; multiply three by four, you get twelve, then make each hundred over twelve, each share is eight and one-third dirhams, so the right of the owner of the property becomes forty shares, and the right of the buyer becomes ninety-nine shares, so the third is one hundred thirty-nine shares, so all the property is four hundred seventeen shares; the right of the owner of the property is forty shares, he received from that thirty-four and three-quarters of a share, because he received from the slave half of its sixth, which is one part out of twelve, so the slave became four hundred fourteen shares, one part out of twelve of it is thirty-four and three-quarters of a share; remaining to complete his right is five and a quarter shares, and the heirs' right is two hundred seventy-eight.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents a complex case known as 'al-arus' (the bride) due to its intricate but clear derivation. The scenario: a testator makes two bequests: (1) all his property to one person, and (2) a directive to sell his slave to another person for 1000 dinars (which is the slave's value) but with a favor (muhabah) of 900 dinars discount, meaning the buyer effectively pays only 100. The heirs do not consent. Since bequests are limited to one-third of the estate, both bequests compete within that one-third. The three Hanafi imams differ in their calculation method: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani each derive the distribution differently. The passage explains each derivation step by step, showing how the shares of the two legatees and the heirs are computed. The key principle: both legatees have equal priority in the one-third, so the third is divided proportionally between them. The calculations involve fractions and finding common denominators. Imam Muhammad's derivation is considered the most cautious (on double the base). The case illustrates the Hanafi approach to resolving conflicts among bequests when the estate is insufficient.

Key Terms
المحاباة (al-muhabah): A sale at a discount below market value, treated as a form of bequest for the difference.
الوصية بجميع المال (al-wasiyyah bi-jami' al-mal): A bequest of the entire estate to one person, which is invalid beyond one-third unless heirs consent.
تخريج (takhrij): Derivation of the ruling by applying legal principles to a specific case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the 'al-arus' case, why did Imam Muhammad double the base numbers in his derivation?
A) To increase the share of the heirs
B) To avoid fractions and ensure the calculation is cautious
C) To give the legatee of the property a larger share
D) Because the heirs consented

Key Takeaway
When multiple bequests exceed one-third, they are divided proportionally within the one-third; the Hanafi imams differ only in the arithmetic method, all being valid.
